Refuting the Superiority of Later Generations over the Salaf
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the notion that later generations exceed the early Muslims in knowledge, especially of Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's refutation of the claim that later generations surpass the Salaf in knowledge of Allah and identify the textual and logical basis for his argument.

Core Idea
Denying the superiority of the Salaf in knowledge of Allah is a disguised form of rejectionism (rafd).

Ibn Taymiyya confronts a dangerous claim: that later generations can surpass the early Muslims (Salaf) in knowledge, especially the highest knowledge of Allah. This passage systematically dismantles that claim using textual evidence from the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. You will learn how to identify the logical structure of his refutation and the consequences of rejecting the primacy of the Salaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
What exactly does the opponent assert about the Salaf? They attribute deficiency, error, or ignorance to the Salaf regarding knowledge, clarity, verification, and gnosis, and claim that later generations are more knowledgeable and virtuous.
The opponent's position is that the Salaf fell short in the greatest matter: knowledge of Allah.
2
Classify the error according to Ibn Taymiyya
He labels this attitude as a branch of rafd (rejectionism), but clarifies that it does not necessarily reach the level of takfir (declaring unbelief) or tafsik (declaring sinfulness). It involves accusing the Salaf of ignorance, error, misguidance, or sins.
This classification shows the severity of the claim even if it avoids outright anathematization.
3
Examine the evidence Ibn Taymiyya provides
He cites Quran, Sunnah, and the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah, along with the hadith that the best centuries are the first three. He also quotes 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud praising the Companions and an unnamed authority stating that the Salaf brought sufficient knowledge and no hidden good appeared after them.
The evidence is drawn from multiple sources to establish certainty.
4
Trace the logical implication of the hadith 'each age is worse'
The Prophet said that no time will come but that the one after it is worse until the end. Therefore, it is impossible for a later time to produce better knowledge of Allah, the greatest matter.
This is a decisive refutation: if each age is worse, later generations cannot surpass the Salaf in knowledge of Allah.
5
Assess the epistemic weight of Ibn Taymiyya's argument
He claims that the superiority of the Salaf is 'known by necessity' (ma'lum bi al-darurah) from the religion. This means rejecting it is not just an error but a contradiction of self-evident Islamic truths, indicating one has been led astray by Allah.
This raises the stakes: the opponent is not merely mistaken but opposes the very foundations of Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالفضيلة في العلم والبيان والتحقيق والعرفان والسلف بالنقص في ذلك والتقصير فيه أو الخطأ والجهل، وغايتهم عندهم أن يقيموا أعذارهم في التقصير والتفريط. ولا ريب أن هذا شعبةٌ من الرّفض، فإنه وإن لم يكن تكفيرًا للسلف كما يقوله من يقوله من الرافضة والخوارج، ولا تفسيقا لهم كما يقوله من يقوله من المعتزلة والزيدية وغيرهم كان تجهيلاً لهم وتخطئة وتضليلا، أو نسبة لهم إلى الذنوب والمعاصي وإن لم يكن فسقا، وزعما أن أهل القرون المفضولة في الشريعة أعلم وأفضل من أهل القرون الفاضلة. ومن المعلوم بالضرورة لمن تدبَّر الكتاب والسنة، وما أتفق عليه أهلُ السنة والجماعة من جميع الطوائف، أن خير قرون هذه الأمة في الأعمال والأقوال والاعتقاد وغيرها من كلّ فضيلة أن خيرها القرن الأول، ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم، كما ثبت ذلك عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من غير وجه وأنهم أفضل من الخلف في كل فضيلة من علم وعمل وإيمان وعقل ودين وبيان وعبادة، وأنهم أولى بالبيان لكلِّ مُشكل هذا لا يدفعه إلا من كابر المعلوم بالضرورة من دين الإسلام، وأضله الله على علم، كما قال عبد الله بن مسعود رَضَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ: «من كان منكم مُسْتَنَّا فليَسْتَنَّ بمن قد مات، فإن الحيَّ لا تُؤمَنُ عليه الفتنة، أولئك أصحاب محمد، أبر هذه الأمة قلوبًا، وأعمقها علما، وأقلُّها تكلُّفا، قوم أختارهم الله الصحبة نبيه، وإقامة دينه ، فاعرفوا لهم حقهم، وتمسكوا بهديهم، فإنهم كانوا على الهَدْي المستقيم. وقال غيره: عليكم بآثار من سَلَف، فإنهم جاؤوا بما يكفي وما يشفي، ولم يحدث بعدهم خيرٌ كامِنٌ لم يعلموه. هذا، وقد قال : لا يأتي زمان إلا والذي بعده شر منه حتى تلقوا ربَّكم، فكيف يحدثُ لنا زمان فيه الخير في أعظم المعلومات وهو معرفة الله تعالى؟! هذا لا يكون أبدًا.
With virtue in knowledge, clarity, verification, and gnosis, and the Salaf (early generations) are deficient in that, or falling short therein, or in error and ignorance, and their ultimate goal is to make excuses for their falling short and negligence. There is no doubt that this is a branch of rejection (rafd), for even if it is not declaring the Salaf to be unbelievers as is said by the Rafidah and Khawarij, nor declaring them sinners as is said by the Mu'tazilah and Zaydiyyah and others, it is declaring them ignorant, erroneous, misled, or attributing sins and disobedience to them, even if not sinfulness, and claiming that the people of the inferior centuries in Shariah are more knowledgeable and better than the people of the virtuous centuries. It is known by necessity to whoever reflects on the Book and the Sunnah, and what Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah from all groups have agreed upon, that the best of the centuries of this nation in deeds, words, belief, and other virtues is the first century, then those who follow them, then those who follow them, as established from the Prophet (peace be upon him) from multiple sources, and that they are better than the later ones in every virtue: knowledge, action, faith, intellect, religion, clarity, and worship, and that they are more entitled to clarify every difficulty. This is rejected only by one who contends with what is known by necessity from the religion of Islam, and whom Allah has led astray knowingly. As 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'Whoever among you wants to follow an example, let him follow the example of those who have died, for the living are not safe from tribulation. Those are the Companions of Muhammad, the best of this nation in heart, the deepest in knowledge, the least pretentious, a people whom Allah chose to accompany His Prophet and establish His religion. Recognize their right and adhere to their guidance, for they were on the straight path.' And another said: 'Hold fast to the traces of those who preceded, for they brought what suffices and cures, and no good hidden after them has occurred that they did not know.' And this: He (peace be upon him) said: 'No time will come but that the one after it is worse than it, until you meet your Lord.' So how can there occur for us a time in which there is good in the greatest of known matters, which is knowledge of Allah Almighty? This will never be.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of those who claim that later generations (khalf) are superior in knowledge, especially in the highest knowledge—knowledge of Allah—compared to the early generations (Salaf). The author, Ibn Taymiyya, begins by describing the position of his opponents: they attribute deficiency, error, or ignorance to the Salaf regarding virtue in knowledge, clarity, verification, and gnosis. Their ultimate goal is to excuse their own shortcomings and negligence. He then labels this attitude as a branch of 'rafd' (rejectionism), though he clarifies that it does not necessarily reach the level of declaring the Salaf as disbelievers (takfir) or sinners (tafsiq), but it does involve accusing them of ignorance, error, misguidance, or sins—and it claims that the people of later, inferior centuries are more knowledgeable and virtuous than those of the earlier virtuous centuries. This, he states, is a severe error. He then provides the definitive Islamic evidence: it is known by necessity from the Qur'an, Sunnah, and the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah that the best of centuries are the first, then the second, then the third, as confirmed by multiple hadith reports (e.g., Bukhari and Muslim). These early generations are superior in every virtue: knowledge, action, faith, intellect, religion, clarity, and worship. They are the most entitled to explain any difficulty. Rejecting this is tantamount to rejecting the self-evident truths of Islam and indicates being led astray by Allah. He supports his argument with the famous statement of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, who praised the Companions as having the best hearts, deepest knowledge, and least pretension, and urged following their guidance. Another unnamed authority (often reported from 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz) adds that the early generations brought sufficient and curative knowledge, and no hidden good has emerged after them that they did not already know. Finally, he invokes the hadith that each successive age is worse, so it is impossible for a later time to produce better knowledge of Allah, the greatest matter. Thus, the claim is conclusively refuted.

Key Terms
السلف
الرفض
خير القرون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what is the status of those who claim that later generations are more knowledgeable than the Salaf?
A) They are classified as unbelievers (kafirun).
B) They are a branch of the rejectionists (rafd).
C) They are excused because they seek truth.
D) They are considered ignorant but not sinful.

Key Takeaway
The claim that later generations surpass the Salaf in knowledge of Allah contradicts self-evident Islamic sources and consensus, and amounts to a subtle form of rejectionism (rafd).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Mulahida's Division of Prophetic Knowledge: Practical vs. Theoretical
Critique of the mulahida's claim that the Prophet did not clarify theoretical truths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the mulahida's argument that the Prophet concealed theoretical truths and refute it using Ibn Taymiyya's Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
The mulahida accept the Prophet's practical guidance but deny his theoretical authority – a fatal split.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya exposes a dangerous epistemological division introduced by the atheist philosophers (mulāḥida). They praise the Prophet's practical law but claim his theoretical knowledge was deficient or concealed. This lesson will help you recognize this argument and understand why it undermines the very foundation of prophetic revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two domains
The mulahida distinguish between practical matters (ethics, politics, worship) and theoretical matters (divine attributes, afterlife, Tawhid). Find the sentence in the translation that begins 'As for the intellectual matters...' and note the division.
This division is key to their claim.
2
Extract the mulahida's claim about the Prophet's knowledge
They say the Prophet 'did not clarify the truth in the chapter of Tawhid' and either concealed it or was unaware. Identify the exact phrasing in the Arabic.
This is the core accusation.
3
Analyze the implication
If the Prophet did not clarify theoretical truths, then revelation is incomplete and philosophy is needed to supplement it. What does this imply about the authority of the Quran and Sunnah?
This is an epistemological challenge.
4
Apply Ibn Taymiyya's refutation
Ibn Taymiyya quotes Quranic verses showing the Prophet was sent with clear signs and light, teaching the Book and wisdom. How do these verses refute the mulahida's claim?
The refutation is revelation-based and logical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما أحسن ما قال الشافعي الله في رسالته: «هم فوقنا في كل علم وعقل ودين وفضل، وكلّ سببٍ يُنال به علم أو يُدْرَكُ به هدى، ورأيهم لنا خيرٌ من رأينا لأنفسنا». وأيضًا، فيقال لهؤلاء - جهميَّةِ الكلابية، كصاحب هذا الكلام أبي محمد وأمثاله : كيف تدَّعون طريقة السَّلف، وغاية ما عند السلف أن يكونوا موافقين لرسول الله ؟! فإن عامَّة ما عند السَّلف من العلم والإيمان ما استفادوه من نبيهم الذي أخرجهم الله به من الظُّلمات إلى النُّور، وهداهم به إلى صراط العزيز الحميد، الذي قال الله فيه : ﴿هُوَ الَّذِي يُنَزِّلُ عَلَى عَبْدِهِ وَايَتٍ بَيِّنَتٍ لِيُخْرِجَكُم مِّنَ الظُّلُمَاتِ إِلَى النُّورِ﴾ [الحديد: 9]، وقال: ﴿يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا اتَّقُوا اللَّهَ وَعَامِنُوا بِرَسُولِهِ يُؤْتِكُمْ كِفْلَيْنِ مِن رَّحْمَتِهِ، وَيَجْعَل لَّكُمْ نُورًا تَمْشُونَ بِهِ، وَيَغْفِرْ لَكُمْ وَاللَّهُ غَفُورٌ رَّحِيمٌ لِئَلَّا يَعْلَمَ أَهْلُ الْكِتَبِ أَلَّا يَقْدِرُونَ عَلَى شَيْءٍ مِّن فَضْلِ اللَّهِ﴾ [الحديد: ۲۸، ۲۹]، وقال: ﴿لَقَدْ مَنَّ اللَّهُ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ إِذْ بَعَثَ فِيهِمْ رَسُولًا مِّنْ أَنفُسِهِمْ يَتْلُوا عَلَيْهِمْ وَايَتِهِ، وَيُزَكِّيهِمْ وَيُعَلِّمُهُمُ الْكِتَابَ وَالْحِكْمَةَ وَإِن كَانُوا مِن قَبْلُ لَفِي ضَلَلٍ مُّبِينٍ﴾ [آل عمران: ١٦٤]، وقال تعالى: ﴿وَكَذَلِكَ أَوْحَيْنَا إِلَيْكَ رُوحًا مِنْ أَمْرِنَا مَا كُنتَ تَدْرِى مَا الْكِتَبُ وَلَا الْإِيمَانُ وَلَكِن جَعَلْتَهُ نُورًا نَهْدِى بِهِ، مَن نَّشَاءُ مِنْ عِبَادِنَا وَإِنَّكَ لَتَهْدِى إِلَى صِرَاطٍ مُّسْتَقِيمٍ ) صِرَاطِ اللَّهِ الَّذِى لَهُ مَا فِي السَّمَوَاتِ وَمَا فِي الْأَرْضِ ﴾ [الشورى ٥٣،٥٢]. وأبو محمد وأمثاله قد سلكوا مسلك الملاحدة الذين يقولون: إن الرسول لم يبين الحق في باب التوحيد، ولا بيَّن للناس ما هو الأمر عليه في نفسه، بل أظهر للناس خلاف الحقِّ، والحقُّ إما كتمه وإما [ أنه ] غير عالم به. فإن هؤلاء الملاحدة من المتفلسفة ومن سلك سبيلهم، المخالفين لما جاء به الرسول في الأمور العلمية، كالتوحيد والمعاد وغير ذلك، يقولون: إن الرسول أحكَمَ الأمور العملية المتعلقة بالأخلاق والسياسة المنزلية والمدنية، وأتى بشريعة عملية هي أفضل شرائع العالم، ويعترفون بأنه لم يقرع العالم ناموس أفضل من ناموسه ولا أكمل منه، فإنهم رأوا حُسْنَ سیاسته للعالم وما أقامه من سُنَن العدل و محاه من الظلم. وأما الأمور العِلمية التي أخبر بها - من صفات الرب، وأسمائه، وملائكته وكتبه ورسله واليوم الآخر ، والجنة والنار ـ فلما رأوهـا تخالف ما هم عليه صاروا في الرسول فريقين: فعلا تهم يقولون: إنه لم يكن يعرفُ هذه المعارف، وإنما كان كماله في الأمور العملية العبادات والأخلاق، وأما الأمور العلمية فالفلاسفة أعلمُ
How excellent is what al-Shafi'i said in his Risala: 'They are above us in every knowledge, intellect, religion, and virtue, and every means by which knowledge is attained or guidance is perceived, and their opinion for us is better than our opinion for ourselves.' Also, it is said to these - the Jahmiyya of the Kullabiyya, like the author of this speech, Abu Muhammad and his likes: How do you claim the way of the Salaf, while the utmost of what the Salaf have is that they were in agreement with the Messenger of Allah? Indeed, the general knowledge and faith that the Salaf have is what they obtained from their Prophet, by whom Allah brought them out of darkness into light and guided them to the path of the Mighty, the Praiseworthy, about whom Allah said: 'He it is Who sends down upon His Servant clear verses that He may bring you out of darkness into the light' [57:9], and He said: 'O you who have believed, fear Allah and believe in His Messenger; He will give you a double portion of His mercy and will make for you a light by which you will walk and forgive you; and Allah is Forgiving and Merciful, that the People of the Scripture may know that they are not able to obtain anything of the bounty of Allah' [57:28-29], and He said: 'Certainly did Allah confer great favor upon the believers when He sent among them a Messenger from themselves, reciting to them His verses and purifying them and teaching them the Book and wisdom, although they were before in manifest error' [3:164], and the Exalted said: 'And thus We have revealed to you an inspiration of Our command. You did not know what the Book is nor what is faith, but We have made it a light by which We guide whom We will of Our servants. And indeed, you guide to a straight path - the path of Allah, to whom belongs whatever is in the heavens and whatever is on the earth' [42:52-53]. And Abu Muhammad and his likes have followed the path of the atheists who say that the Messenger did not clarify the truth in the chapter of Tawhid, nor did he explain to people what the matter is in itself, but rather he showed people the contrary of the truth, and the truth he either concealed or he was unaware of it. Indeed, these atheists from the philosophers and those who follow their way, who oppose what the Messenger brought in matters of knowledge, such as Tawhid, the afterlife, and so on, say that the Messenger perfected the practical matters related to ethics, domestic and civil politics, and brought a practical law that is the best of the world's laws, and they acknowledge that the best law that has struck the world is his law, nor is there anything more perfect than it, for they saw the goodness of his governance of the world and what he established of the customs of justice and the elimination of injustice. As for the intellectual matters he informed about - the attributes of the Lord, His names, His angels, His books, His messengers, the Last Day, Paradise, and Hell - when they saw that they contradict what they hold, they became two groups regarding the Messenger: some of them say that he did not know these knowledges, and that his perfection was only in practical matters of worship and ethics, and as for intellectual matters, the philosophers are more knowledgeable.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of those who claim to follow the Salaf while actually adopting the position of the atheist philosophers (mulāḥida) who deny that the Prophet (peace be upon him) clarified the truth in theological matters. The author begins by quoting al-Shāfiʿī's praise of the Salaf (the early Muslims) to establish their authority. He then addresses those he calls the Jahmiyya al-Kullābiyya, led by Abu Muhammad (likely Ibn Kullāb or a follower), who claim to follow the Salaf's method. The author points out the inconsistency: the Salaf's knowledge and faith came exclusively from the Prophet, whom Allah sent with clear signs and light. He cites several Quranic verses to emphasize that the Prophet brought people out of darkness and taught them the Book and wisdom. Then he attacks Abu Muhammad and his ilk for following the path of the mulāḥida. These atheists acknowledge the Prophet's excellence in practical matters (ethics, politics) but claim that in theoretical matters (theology, divine attributes, afterlife), he either concealed the truth or was ignorant, thus elevating philosophers above the Prophet. The author thus identifies a dangerous epistemological split: practical knowledge from the Prophet is accepted, but theoretical knowledge is attributed to the philosophers. This critique aims to defend the prophetic revelation as the sole source of truth in both practical and theoretical domains.

Key Terms
جهمية الكلابية
ملاحدة
طريقة السلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do the mulāḥida claim about the Prophet's knowledge in theoretical matters?
A) He was the most knowledgeable in all matters.
B) He either concealed it or was unaware of it.
C) He taught it to the philosophers.
D) He only taught practical matters.

Key Takeaway
The mulahida's split between practical and theoretical prophetic authority is a direct attack on the comprehensiveness of revelation; Ibn Taymiyya refutes it by affirming that the Prophet brought light and guidance in all matters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Task 2: Identify any contemporary Muslim thinker who implicitly or explicitly claims that the Prophet only addressed practical matters. Discuss how Ibn Taymiyya's critique applies.

Claiming Salafiyya While Rejecting Salaf's Source of Knowledge
Critique of the Jahmiyya-Kullabiyya for inconsistency in claiming Salaf's method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the inconsistency in the Jahmiyya-Kullabiyya's claim to follow the Salaf while denying the Prophet's theoretical authority, and explain why this is a logical contradiction.

Core Idea
You cannot claim to follow the Salaf while rejecting the very source of their knowledge: the Prophet.

Ibn Taymiyya points out a glaring contradiction: the Jahmiyya-Kullabiyya claim to follow the way of the Salaf, yet they adopt the mulahida's position that the Prophet did not clarify theoretical truths. But the Salaf derived all their knowledge from the Prophet. This lesson dissects this inconsistency and shows why it is unsustainable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the group being addressed
Ibn Taymiyya addresses the Jahmiyya al-Kullabiyya, represented by Abu Muhammad and his followers. Find the Arabic phrase that names them.
Abu Muhammad is likely Ibn Kullab or a follower.
2
Extract their claim
They claim to follow the way of the Salaf (ṭarīqat al-salaf). Note the phrase and its significance.
This claim gives them credibility.
3
Identify the source of Salaf's knowledge
Ibn Taymiyya asserts that the Salaf's knowledge and faith came exclusively from the Prophet. He quotes Quranic verses to prove this. What do these verses emphasize?
The Prophet brought light, taught Book and wisdom.
4
Recognize the contradiction
The Jahmiyya-Kullabiyya [like Abu Muhammad] follow the mulahida who say the Prophet did not clarify theoretical truths. If the Salaf's knowledge depends on the Prophet, then denying the Prophet's theoretical authority undermines the Salaf's own knowledge. Why is this a logical contradiction?
They cannot consistently hold both positions.

These atheists acknowledge the Prophet's excellence in practical matters (ethics, politics) but claim that in theoretical matters (theology, divine attributes, afterlife), he either concealed the truth or was ignorant, thus elevating philosophers above the Prophet. The author thus identifies a dangerous epistemological split: practical knowledge from the Prophet is accepted, but theoretical knowledge is attributed to the philosophers. This critique aims to defend the prophetic revelation as the sole source of truth in both practical and theoretical domains.

Key Terms
جهمية الكلابية
ملاحدة
طريقة السلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the central contradiction Ibn Taymiyya identifies in the Jahmiyya-Kullabiyya?
A) They claim to follow the Salaf but deny the Prophet's authority in practical matters.
B) They claim to follow the Salaf but adopt the mulahida's view that the Prophet did not clarify theoretical truths.
C) They claim to follow the Salaf but reject the Quran.
D) They claim to follow the Salaf but are actually philosophers.

Key Takeaway
Claiming to follow the Salaf while denying the Prophet's comprehensive authority is a logical and methodological contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: In a few sentences, reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument that the Jahmiyya-Kullabiyya's claim is self-contradictory. Identify the two incompatible positions.
?
Task 2: Find an example from contemporary Islamic discourse where a group claims to follow the Salaf but adopts a theological or legal position that contradicts the clear teachings of the Quran and Sunnah. How would Ibn Taymiyya's critique apply?

Ibn Taymiyya's Refutation of Philosophical Superiority over Prophethood
Ibn Taymiyya critiques philosophers who claim the Prophet concealed theoretical truths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the philosophers' claim about the Prophet's theoretical knowledge and evaluate its internal consistency.

Core Idea
Philosophers admit the Prophet's practical excellence but deny his theoretical knowledge — a contradiction Ibn Taymiyya exposes.

In this passage from Naqd al-Mantiq, Ibn Taymiyya confronts a dangerous claim: that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) either concealed or was ignorant of theoretical truths like tawhid and the afterlife. The philosophers, according to Ibn Taymiyya, acknowledge the Prophet's superiority in practical matters but elevate themselves in theoretical knowledge. Your task is to dissect his argument and see how he turns their own admissions against them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the philosophers' concession
Find the part where Ibn Taymiyya notes that the philosophers admit the Prophet's excellence in practical matters: ethics, domestic and civil politics, and his law being the best. This is their starting point.
The concession is in the middle of the passage: 'they acknowledge that the world has not seen a law better than his law'.
2
Identify their criticism
Locate the claim that the Prophet did not know theoretical matters such as the attributes of God, the afterlife, etc. The philosophers say he either concealed or was ignorant of these.
This is at the beginning and later: 'he did not know these knowledges'.
3
Pinpoint the logical inconsistency
Ibn Taymiyya shows that if the Prophet is perfect in practical matters (ethics, governance), he must be even more perfect in theoretical matters, which are higher. The philosophers' partial praise leads to a contradiction.
The inconsistency is not stated explicitly but is implied by the contrast.
4
Evaluate the extreme implications
Note that some philosophers go further, claiming that 'Ali and Harun were more knowledgeable than the Prophet and Moses, and venerating Pharaoh. This shows the absurd consequences of their position.
Ibn Taymiyya uses reductio ad absurdum by highlighting these claims.
5
Assess Ibn Taymiyya's rhetorical strategy
He uses their own admissions against them: they praise the Prophet's practical achievements, so they cannot consistently deny his theoretical knowledge. The critique is both logical and rhetorical.
This is a common jadal (dialectical) technique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأبو محمد وأمثاله قد سلكوا مسلك الملاحدة الذين يقولون: إن الرسول لم يبين الحق في باب التوحيد، ولا بيَّن للناس ما هو الأمر عليه في نفسه، بل أظهر للناس خلاف الحقِّ، والحقُّ إما كتمه وإما [ أنه ] غير عالم به. فإن هؤلاء الملاحدة من المتفلسفة ومن سلك سبيلهم، المخالفين لما جاء به الرسول في الأمور العلمية، كالتوحيد والمعاد وغير ذلك، يقولون: إن الرسول أحكَمَ الأمور العملية المتعلقة بالأخلاق والسياسة المنزلية والمدنية، وأتى بشريعة عملية هي أفضل شرائع العالم، ويعترفون بأنه لم يقرع العالم ناموس أفضل من ناموسه ولا أكمل منه، فإنهم رأوا حُسْنَ سیاسته للعالم وما أقامه من سُنَن العدل و محاه من الظلم. وأما الأمور العِلمية التي أخبر بها - من صفات الرب، وأسمائه، وملائكته وكتبه ورسله واليوم الآخر ، والجنة والنار ـ فلما رأوهـا تخالف ما هم عليه صاروا في الرسول فريقين: فعلا تهم يقولون: إنه لم يكن يعرفُ هذه المعارف، وإنما كان كماله في الأمور العملية العبادات والأخلاق، وأما الأمور العلمية فالفلاسفة أعلم بها منه، بل ومن غيره من الأنبياء. وهؤلاء يقولون : إن عليا كان فيلسوفا وأنه كان أعلم بالعِلميات من الرسول، وأن هارون كان فيلسوفا وكان أعلم بالعلميات من موسى، وكثير منهم يعظم فرعون ويسمونه أفلاطون القبطي، ويدعون أن صاحب مدين الذي تزوج موسى أبنته، الذي يقول بعض الناس: إنه شعيب، يقـول وهو غلط شاع عند كثير من الناس الذين لا خبرة لهم بحقائق العلم ودلائله وطرقه السمعية والعقلية كما قال المصنف.
And Abu Muhammad and his likes have followed the path of the atheists who say: The Messenger did not clarify the truth concerning the matter of tawhid, nor did he make clear to people what the matter is in itself, rather he showed people contrary to the truth, and the truth—either he concealed it or he was not knowledgeable of it. For these atheists among the philosophers and those who follow their path, who oppose what the Messenger brought regarding theoretical matters, such as tawhid and the resurrection and other than that, say: The Messenger mastered the practical matters related to ethics and domestic and civil politics, and brought a practical law that is the best of the world's laws, and they acknowledge that the world has not seen a law better than his law nor more complete than it, for they saw the excellence of his governance of the world and what he established of the norms of justice and the elimination of injustice. As for the theoretical matters he informed of—from the attributes of the Lord, His names, His angels, His books, His messengers, the Last Day, Paradise and Hellfire—when they saw that they contradicted what they themselves held, they became two groups concerning the Messenger: one group says that he did not know these knowledges, and that his perfection was only in practical matters of worship and ethics, and as for theoretical matters, the philosophers are more knowledgeable of them than he, and indeed than other prophets. And these say: 'Ali was a philosopher and he was more knowledgeable in theoretical matters than the Messenger, and Harun was a philosopher and more knowledgeable in theoretical matters than Moses, and many of them venerate Pharaoh and call him the Coptic Plato, and they claim that the companion of Madyan whose daughter Moses married—whom some people say is Shu'ayb—says, and this is an error that has become widespread among many people who have no experience with the realities of knowledge, its evidences, and its auditory and rational methods, as the author said.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This is a critical passage from Ibn Taymiyya's Naqd al-Mantiq in which he refutes the claims of philosophers and their followers who elevate philosophical knowledge above prophetic revelation. Ibn Taymiyya begins by accusing Abu Muhammad (likely a specific philosopher or group) and his ilk of following the path of the atheists (malāhida). These atheists claim that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) did not clarify the truth in matters of tawhid (divine unity) and that he either concealed the truth or was ignorant of it. The passage then explains that these philosophers acknowledge the Prophet's excellence in practical affairs—ethics, domestic and civil politics—and consider his revealed law the best ever, but they deny his knowledge in theoretical matters such as the attributes of God, the afterlife, etc. They claim that the Prophet's perfection was only in practical matters of worship and ethics, and that philosophers are more knowledgeable in theoretical matters, even more so than other prophets. Ibn Taymiyya then exposes the extreme consequences of this view: some claim that 'Ali ibn Abi Talib was a philosopher more learned than the Prophet, and that Harun was more learned than Moses. Furthermore, they venerate Pharaoh, calling him the 'Coptic Plato,' and spread false claims about the prophet Shu'ayb. Ibn Taymiyya dismisses these as errors prevalent among those ignorant of true knowledge and its methods.

Key Terms
ملاحدة
المتفلسفة
الأمور العلمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do the philosophers (mutafalsifa) claim about the Prophet's knowledge of theoretical matters?
A) He knew everything and taught it all clearly.
B) He was more knowledgeable than the philosophers in both practical and theoretical matters.
C) He did not know these knowledges, and his perfection was only in practical matters.
D) He concealed theoretical matters because the people were not ready.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya exposes the internal contradiction of philosophers who praise the Prophet's practical perfection yet deny his theoretical knowledge, showing that their position leads to absurdities that undermine the very respect they claim for him.

Philosophers' False Claims About Prophets
Ibn Taymiyya refutes philosophers' claims that prophets were philosophers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the specific historical errors Ibn Taymiyya exposes in the philosophers' claims about prophets.

Core Idea
Philosophers' claim that prophets were philosophers is both historically false and theologically corrupt.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya attacks the philosophers' audacious claims that the prophets were philosophers and even superior to the Messengers in rational knowledge. He exposes the absurdity of these claims by pointing to the philosophers' ignorance of prophetic history. By the end of this lesson, you will see how Ibn Taymiyya uses factual historical knowledge to dismantle these false narratives.

Guided Path
1
List the philosophers' claims
Identify each claim about prophets mentioned: Ali was a philosopher and more knowledgeable than the Prophet, Harun was a philosopher and more knowledgeable than Musa, Pharaoh is the Coptic Plato, Shu'ayb is Plato, Aristotle is al-Khidr.
These claims are listed at the beginning of the passage.
2
Identify Ibn Taymiyya's response
Notice that he dismisses them as ignorance and then focuses on one historical error – the confusion between Alexander and Dhul-Qarnayn – as an example of their deeper ignorance.
He says the least of their errors is ignorance of prophetic history.
3
Analyze the corrective method
See how he uses historical facts (dates, locations, beliefs) to refute. For example, he notes that Aristotle lived 300 years before Christ, that Alexander did not build the barrier, and that Dhul-Qarnayn was a monotheist.
Compare the factual corrections Ibn Taymiyya provides.
4
Apply to a similar claim
If someone claims a prophet was a philosopher, how would you refute using Ibn Taymiyya's method? Consider historical evidence and theological compatibility.
This step requires synthesizing Ibn Taymiyya's approach.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهؤلاء يقولون : إن عليا كان فيلسوفا وأنه كان أعلم بالعِلميات من الرسول، وأن هارون كان فيلسوفا وكان أعلم بالعلميات من موسى، وكثير منهم يعظم فرعون ويسمونه أفلاطون القبطي، ويدعون أن صاحب مدين الذي تزوج موسى أبنته، الذي يقول بعض الناس: إنه شعيب، يقول هؤلاء: إنه أفلاطون أستاذ أرسطو، ويقولون: إن أرسطو هو الخَضِر . إلى أمثال هذا الكلام الذي فيه من الجهل والضلال ما لا يعلمه إلا ذو الجلال، أقل ما فيه جهلهم بتواريخ الأنبياء، فإن أرسطو باتفاقهم كان وزير الإسكندر بن فيلبس المقدوني الذي تؤرّخ له اليهود والنصارى التاريخ الرُّومي، وكان قبل المسيح بنحو ثلاثمئة سنة. وقد يظنُّون أن هذا هو ذو القرنين المذكور في القرآن، وأن أرسطو كان وزيرا لذي القرنين المذكور في القرآن. وهذا جهل؛ فإن هذا الإسكندر بن فيلبس لم يصل إلى بلاد الترك، ولم يَبْنِ السَّدَّ، وإنما وصل إلى بلاد الفرس. وذو القرنين المذكورُ في القرآن وصل إلى شرق الأرض وغربها، وكان متقدما على هذا ، يقال : اسمه الإسكندر بن دارا، وكان موحدا مؤمنًا، وذاك مشركًا كان يعبد هو وقومه الكواكب والأصنام، ويُعانون السحر، كما كان أرسطو وقومه من اليونان مشركين يعبدون الأصنام ويُعَانُون السِّحر، ولهم في ذلك مصنفات، وأخبارهم مشهورة، وآثارهم ظاهرة بذلك، فأين هذا من هذا ؟!
And these people say: 'Ali was a philosopher and that he was more knowledgeable in the rational sciences than the Messenger, and that Harun was a philosopher and was more knowledgeable in the rational sciences than Musa.' And many of them venerate Pharaoh and call him the Coptic Plato. And they claim that the companion of Madyan whose daughter Musa married—whom some people say is Shu'ayb—these people say: 'He is Plato, the teacher of Aristotle.' And they say: 'Aristotle is al-Khidr.' To such speech, which contains ignorance and misguidance unknown except to the Possessor of Majesty. The least of it is their ignorance of the histories of the prophets. For Aristotle, by their agreement, was the vizier of Alexander son of Philip the Macedonian, from whom the Jews and Christians date the Roman calendar, and he was about three hundred years before Christ. And they may suppose that this is Dhul-Qarnayn mentioned in the Qur'an, and that Aristotle was the vizier of Dhul-Qarnayn mentioned in the Qur'an. This is ignorance; for this Alexander son of Philip did not reach the land of the Turks, nor did he build the barrier. Rather, he only reached the land of Persia. And Dhul-Qarnayn mentioned in the Qur'an reached the east of the earth and its west, and he was before this one. It is said: his name is Alexander son of Dara, and he was a monotheist believer. And that other one was a polytheist—he and his people worshipped the planets and idols and practiced sorcery—just as Aristotle and his people among the Greeks were polytheists, worshipping idols and practicing sorcery. They have authored works on that, and their reports are well-known, and their traces are manifest in that. So where is this from that?!
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of absurd historical and theological claims made by certain philosophers (likely the Peripatetic Muslims or those influenced by Greek thought). He begins by listing their claims: that 'Ali was a philosopher superior to the Prophet Muhammad, that Harun was a philosopher superior to Musa, that Pharaoh is the Coptic Plato, that Shu'ayb is Plato the teacher of Aristotle, and that Aristotle is al-Khidr. Ibn Taymiyya dismisses these as ignorant and misguided, emphasizing that the least problem is their ignorance of prophetic history. He then tackles the confusion between Alexander the Great (son of Philip) and the Qur'anic figure Dhul-Qarnayn. By agreement, Aristotle was the vizier of Alexander son of Philip, who lived about 300 years before Christ. Some mistakenly think this Alexander is Dhul-Qarnayn, and that Aristotle was his vizier. Ibn Taymiyya corrects this: Alexander son of Philip never reached the land of the Turks nor built the barrier; he only reached Persia. Dhul-Qarnayn, however, reached the East and West, lived earlier (said to be Alexander son of Dara), and was a monotheist. In contrast, Alexander son of Philip was a polytheist, worshipping celestial bodies and idols, and practicing sorcery—just like Aristotle and the Greeks. Ibn Taymiyya contrasts the two figures and concludes by asking rhetorically, 'Where is this from that?!'—meaning how can one confuse the two? The passage is a classic example of Ibn Taymiyya's method: exposing the ignorance of philosophers in historical and religious matters, and defending the integrity of prophetic figures and Qur'anic narratives.

Key Terms
فيلسوف
أفلاطون القبطي
ذو القرنين

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Their veneration of Pharaoh
B) Their ignorance of the histories of the prophets
C) Their claim that Ali was a philosopher
D) Their claim that Aristotle was al-Khidr

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya uses historical facts to refute the philosophers' false claims about prophets, exposing their ignorance of prophetic history.

Distinguishing Dhul-Qarnayn from Alexander the Great
Ibn Taymiyya corrects the misidentification of Alexander as Dhul-Qarnayn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish Dhul-Qarnayn from Alexander the Great based on Ibn Taymiyya's historical and theological criteria.

Core Idea
Conflating polytheist Alexander with monotheist Dhul-Qarnayn is a sign of deep historical ignorance.

One of the most egregious errors of the philosophers is confusing the Qur'anic figure Dhul-Qarnayn with Alexander the Great. Ibn Taymiyya clarifies the immense differences between the two: one was a monotheist who reached the ends of the earth, the other a polytheist who never went beyond Persia. This lesson will equip you to recognize and refute this common confusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two figures conflated
Note the two distinct individuals: Alexander son of Philip (Alexander the Great) and Dhul-Qarnayn (said to be Alexander son of Dara). Ibn Taymiyya argues they are not the same.
The philosophers mistakenly think the same Alexander is Dhul-Qarnayn.
2
Compare their attributes
Ibn Taymiyya contrasts: Alexander son of Philip did not reach the land of the Turks, did not build the barrier, only reached Persia, and was a polytheist. Dhul-Qarnayn reached east and west, built the barrier, lived earlier, and was a monotheist.
Use a table to list the differences.
3
Identify the theological significance
Why does this matter? Confusing a polytheist with a Qur'anic hero misrepresents the Qur'anic narrative and undermines the integrity of the revelation.
Ibn Taymiyya is defending the sanctity of the Qur'anic account.
4
Formulate a refutation
Based on Ibn Taymiyya's criteria, construct a brief rebuttal: Dhul-Qarnayn was a monotheist and reached the barrier; Alexander was a polytheist and did not. Therefore they are different.
This can be used in discussions or polemics.

The Bāṭiniyya's Doctrine of Allegorical Deception
Ibn Taymiyya exposes the Bāṭiniyya's distortion of revelation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Bāṭiniyya's claim that the Prophet concealed true doctrines and used allegory, and reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's critique of this claim.

Core Idea
The Bāṭiniyya accuse the Prophet of deception; Ibn Taymiyya refutes this by exposing their own deception.

This passage from Ibn Taymiyya's Naqd al-Mantiq targets one of the most dangerous claims of the esoteric philosophers: that the Prophet knew the truth about God and the afterlife but deliberately concealed it from the masses, giving them only allegories. Why would a Prophet do that? The Bāṭiniyya claim it was for their own good. Ibn Taymiyya shows this is actually an accusation of fraud and a distortion of revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Bāṭiniyya's claim about the Prophet's knowledge
Read the first part of the passage where Ibn Taymiyya describes what the second group says: the Prophet knew the true doctrines (e.g., God has no positive attributes, no resurrection of bodies) but could not reveal them openly.
2
Extract the justification they offer for concealment
They claim the common people could not accept the truth, so the Prophet used allegory (takhīl wa tamthīl) for their benefit, even though it involved deception.
Note the term 'al-takhīl wa al-tamthīl' – allegory and representation.
3
Recognize Ibn Taymiyya's implicit critique
Ibn Taymiyya does not directly refute here but juxtaposes their claim with the statement that this involves 'talbīs' (deception) and 'tajhīl' (ignorance) – implying the Prophet would not do such a thing.
The critique is built into the description; Ibn Taymiyya expects the reader to see the problem.
4
Articulate the core refutation
The Bāṭiniyya's claim directly contradicts the prophetic mission of clear guidance and honesty. If the Prophet knew the true doctrines, he would have taught them openly; the idea that he hid them is an accusation of fraud.
This is the standard Islamic rejection of esoteric interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمقصود هنا بيان ما يقوله هؤلاء الفلاسفة الباطنية فيما جاء به الرسول. والفريق الثاني منهم يقولون : إن الرسول كان يعلم الحقَّ الثابت في نفس الأمر في التوحيد والمعاد، ويعرفُ أن الرب ليس له صفةٌ ثبوتية، وأنه لا يرى ولا يتكلَّم، وأن الأفلاك قديمةٌ أزلية لم تزل ولا تزال، وأن الأبدان لا تعود، ولكن يقول بما عليه هؤلاء الباطنية في الباطن، لكن ما كان يمكنه إظهار ذلك للعامة؛ لأن هذا إذا ظهر لم تقبله عقولهم وقلوبهم، بل يُنْكِرون وينْفِرون، فأظهر لهم من التخييل والتمثيل ما ينتفعون به في دينهم، وإن كان في ذلك تلبيس عليهم وتجهيل لهم واعتقادهم الأمر على خلاف ما هو عليه، لما في ذلك من المصلحة لهم. ويجعلون أئمة الباطنية، كبني عبيد بن ميمون القَدَّاح الذين أدعوا أنهم من ولد محمد بن إسماعيل بن جعفر، ولم يكونوا من أولاده، بل كان جدهم يهوديًا ربيبًا لمجوسي، وأظهروا التشيع، ولم يكونوا في الحقيقة على دين واحد من الشيعة لا الإمامية ولا الزيدية، بل ولا الغالية الذين يعتقدون إلهية عليّ أو نبوته، بل كانوا شرا من هؤلاء كلهم؛ ولهذا كثر تصانيف المسلمين في كشف أسرارهم وهتك أستارهم، وكثر غزو المسلمين لهم، وقصصهم معروفة. وابن سينا وأهل بيته كانوا من أتباع هؤلاء على عهد حاكمهم المصري؛ ولهذا دخل أبن سينا في الفلسفة. وهؤلاء يجعلون محمد بن إسماعيل هو الإمام المكتوم، وأنه نسخ شرع محمد بن عبد الله بن عبد المطلب، ويقولون: إن هؤلاء الإسماعيلية كانوا أئمة معصومين، بل قد يقولون: إنهم أفضل من الأنبياء، وقد يقولون: إنهم آلهة يُعبدون. ولهذا أرسل الحاكم غلامه نشتكين الدرزي إلى وادي تيم الله بن ثعلبة بالشام، فأضل أهل تلك الناحية، وبقاياهم فيهم إلى اليوم يقولون
The aim here is to explain what these esoteric philosophers say regarding what the Prophet brought. The second group among them says: The Prophet knew the true reality in itself concerning tawḥīd and the afterlife, and he knew that the Lord has no positive attribute, that He is not seen nor speaks, that the celestial spheres are eternal without beginning and will never cease, and that bodies do not return [at resurrection]. But he spoke according to what these esotericists hold inwardly, yet he could not make that apparent to the common people; because if this became apparent, their minds and hearts would not accept it; rather, they would deny and recoil. So he presented to them through allegory and representation what would benefit them in their religion, even if that involved deception and ignorance for them and their belief in the matter being contrary to what it is, because of the benefit that was in that for them. And they regard the imams of the esotericists, like the Banū ʿUbayd ibn Maymūn al-Qaddāḥ who claimed to be from the offspring of Muḥammad ibn Ismāʿīl ibn Jaʿfar, but they were not from his descendants; rather, their ancestor was a Jewish stepchild of a Magian. They outwardly displayed Shīʿism, but in reality they were not committed to any one of the Shīʿa sects, neither the Imāmiyya nor the Zaydiyya, nor even the extremists who believe in the divinity of ʿAlī or his prophethood; rather, they were worse than all of them. For this reason, the Muslims' authored works increased in exposing their secrets and tearing their veils, and the Muslims' campaigns against them increased, and their stories are well-known. And Ibn Sīnā and his household were among the followers of these people at the time of their Egyptian ruler; for this reason Ibn Sīnā entered into philosophy. And these people make Muḥammad ibn Ismāʿīl the hidden Imam, and that he abrogated the sharīʿa of Muḥammad ibn ʿAbdullāh ibn ʿAbd al-Muṭṭalib, and they say that these Ismāʿīlīs are infallible imams; indeed they may say that they are better than the prophets, and they may say that they are gods who are worshipped. For this reason al-Ḥākim sent his servant Nashtakīn al-Darazī to the valley of Taymillāh ibn Thaʿlaba in Syria, and he led astray the people of that region, and their remnants among them to this day say...
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is a critical exposé by Ibn Taymiyya of the Bāṭiniyya (esoteric) philosophers. He begins by stating that the purpose is to explain what these philosophers claim regarding what the Prophet brought. Then he describes their view that the Prophet knew the true doctrines (like denial of divine attributes, denial of bodily resurrection, etc.) but concealed them from the public. They claim he used allegory and representation for their benefit, which amounts to deception. This is a refutation of their claim that the Prophet was an esotericist. Next, he discusses the leaders of the Bāṭiniyya, specifically the descendants of ʿUbayd ibn Maymūn al-Qaddāḥ, who falsely claimed descent from Muḥammad ibn Ismāʿīl. He notes their true origins as a Jewish stepchild of a Magian, and that they outwardly professed Shīʿism but were worse than all Shīʿa sects. Muslim scholars have written many works exposing them, and Muslims fought them. Then he states that Ibn Sīnā and his household were followers of these Bāṭiniyya during the time of the Egyptian ruler al-Ḥākim, explaining why Ibn Sīnā entered philosophy. Finally, he describes their extreme beliefs: that Muḥammad ibn Ismāʿīl is the hidden Imam who abrogated the sharīʿa, and that the imams are infallible, even superior to prophets or worshipped as gods. He links this to the mission of al-Ḥākim's servant Nashtakīn al-Darazī, who led astray the people of Wādī Taymillāh, and whose remnants still hold these beliefs. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each point as a critique of the Bāṭiniyya's distortion of revelation and their historical connection to the philosophical tradition.

Key Terms
الفلاسفة الباطنية
التخييل والتمثيل
الإسماعيلية
الحاكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what did the Bāṭiniyya claim about the Prophet's knowledge?
A) The Prophet was ignorant of the true doctrines.
B) The Prophet knew the true doctrines and taught them openly to all.
C) The Prophet knew the true doctrines but concealed them from the common people.
D) The Prophet invented the true doctrines himself.

Key Takeaway
The Bāṭiniyya's claim that the Prophet used allegory to hide true doctrines amounts to accusing him of deception, which is a serious distortion of revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify in your own words the Bāṭiniyya's claim about the Prophet's use of allegory. Then, using Ibn Taymiyya's implicit critique, write a refutation from an Ash'ari perspective, showing why the Prophet would not deceive.
?
Find another example in Islamic history where a group used allegorical interpretation to justify extreme doctrines. How would Ibn Taymiyya's critique apply to that case?

Historical Roots of the Bāṭiniyya and Ibn Sīnā's Connection
Ibn Taymiyya exposes the Bāṭiniyya's distortion of revelation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the historical lineage of the Bāṭiniyya imams as described by Ibn Taymiyya and explain Ibn Sīnā's connection to them.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya exposes the Bāṭiniyya as a political movement with fabricated lineages, and links Ibn Sīnā to their circle.

After exposing their doctrine, Ibn Taymiyya turns to the historical reality: the so-called imams of the Bāṭiniyya were impostors with false genealogies. He then reveals that the famous philosopher Ibn Sīnā was a follower of these people. This lesson will help you understand how Ibn Taymiyya uses historical critique to undermine the credibility of both the Bāṭiniyya and the philosophical tradition associated with them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Bāṭiniyya's leadership
Ibn Taymiyya names the Banū ʿUbayd ibn Maymūn al-Qaddāḥ as the leaders of the Bāṭiniyya. Note their claim: they said they were descendants of Muḥammad ibn Ismāʿīl ibn Jaʿfar.
2
Examine Ibn Taymiyya's refutation of their lineage
He states they were not from his descendants; rather, their ancestor was a Jewish stepchild of a Magian. This delegitimizes their claim to religious authority.
Ibn Taymiyya uses genealogical criticism to undermine their spiritual authority.
3
Analyze their religious affiliation
They outwardly showed Shi'ism but were not committed to any Shi'a sect, not even the extremists (ghulat). Ibn Taymiyya says they were worse than all of them.
This shows they were not a legitimate Islamic sect but a politically motivated group.
4
Connect Ibn Sīnā to the Bāṭiniyya
Ibn Taymiyya states that Ibn Sīnā and his household were followers of these people at the time of the Egyptian ruler (al-Ḥākim). This explains why Ibn Sīnā entered philosophy—he was part of their circle.
This link is crucial for Ibn Taymiyya's critique of philosophy: he traces it to a deviant sect.
5
Summarize the extreme doctrines of the Bāṭiniyya
They believe Muḥammad ibn Ismāʿīl is the hidden Imam who abrogated the Sharīʿa, and that their imams are infallible, even superior to prophets or gods. This shows the extent of their deviation.
These doctrines justify political and religious authority outside the mainstream.

Critiquing Esotericist Antinomianism
Ibn Taymiyya exposes the antinomian consequences of Isma'ili esotericism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to deconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's critique of esoteric epistemology that leads to the abandonment of Shari'a obligations.

Core Idea
When knowledge is reserved for an elite, religious obligations become optional.

Ibn Taymiyya here exposes how a sect's claim to secret, superior knowledge can unravel the entire fabric of Islamic law. He argues that the Isma'ilis, following atheist philosophers, use a gradual initiation to strip away obligations, showing that extreme esotericism is not just a theological error but a direct attack on the Shari'a itself. This lesson equips you to recognise and refute such epistemic distortions using Ibn Taymiyya's method.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target sect
Locate the specific group Ibn Taymiyya is critiquing: the Isma'ilis, especially the Druze under al-Hakim. Note the historical details he provides (e.g., Nashtakin al-Darazi).
This sets the concrete context for the critique.
2
Extract the epistemological claim
Find the core belief: that secret 'knowledge of their secrets' perfects the soul, making Shari'a obligations unnecessary for the elite. This is the epistemic justification for antinomianism.
Ibn Taymiyya attributes this to 'atheist philosophers' (al-falāsifa al-malāḥida).
3
Trace the practical outcome
Identify the consequences: the initiate is led step by step from Shi'ism to full abandonment of prayer, fasting, Hajj, and prohibitions. This shows the real-world impact of the epistemological error.
The antinomian conclusion is the logical result of the esoteric premise.
4
Assess the critique's validity
Evaluate Ibn Taymiyya's argument: does he show that the Isma'ili epistemology necessarily leads to antinomianism? Consider whether his evidence (historical reports and statements) supports the causal link.
He is not attacking all esotericism, but a specific system that makes obligations contingent on secret knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقصصهم معروفة. وابن سينا وأهل بيته كانوا من أتباع هؤلاء على عهد حاكمهم المصري؛ ولهذا دخل أبن سينا في الفلسفة (١). وهؤلاء يجعلون محمد بن إسماعيل هو الإمام المكتوم، وأنه نسخ شرع محمد بن عبد الله بن عبد المطلب، ويقولون: إن هؤلاء الإسماعيلية كانوا أثمة معصومين، بل قد يقولون: إنهم أفضل من الأنبياء، وقد يقولون: إنهم آلهة يعبدون. ولهذا أرسل الحاكم غلامه نشتكين (۲) الدرزي إلى وادي تيم الله بن ثعلبة بالشام (۳)، فأضل أهل تلك الناحية، وبقاياهم فيهم إلى اليوم يقولون بإلهية الحاكم، وقد أخرجهم عن دين الإسلام، فلا يرون الصلوات الخمس، ولا صيام شهر رمضان، ولا حج البيت الحرام، ولا تحريم ما حرمه الله ورسوله من الميتة والدم ولحم الخنزير والخمر وغير ذلك. وهؤلاء يأمرون (۱) المستجيب لهم أولا إلى التشيع والتزام ما توجبه الرافضة وتحريم ما يحرمونه، ثم بعد هذا ينقلونه درجة بعد درجة حتى ينقلونه في الآخر إلى الانسلاخ من الإسلام، وأن المقصود هو معرفة أسرارهم، وهو العلم الذي به تكمل النفس، كما تقوله الفلاسفة الملاحدة، فمن حصل له هذا العلم وصل إلى الغاية، وسقطت عنه العبادات التي تجب على العامة، كالصلوات الخمس وصيام رمضان وحج البيت، وحلت له المحرمات التي لا تحل لغيره. فهؤلاء يجعلون الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا عظموه وقالوا: كان كاملا في العلم = من جنس رؤوسهم الملاحدة، وأنه كان يظهر للعامة خلاف ما يبطنه للخاصة. وقد بينا من فساد أقوالهم في غير هذا الموضع ما لا يناسبه هذا المقام (۲).
And their stories are well-known. Ibn Sina and his household were among the followers of these people during the era of their Egyptian ruler; and for this reason Ibn Sina entered into philosophy (1). These people make Muhammad ibn Isma'il the hidden Imam, and that he abrogated the Shari'a of Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Abd al-Muttalib. They say: These Isma'ilis were infallible imams; rather they may say: They are better than the prophets, and they may say: They are gods worshipped. For this reason the ruler sent his servant Nashtakin (2) al-Darazi to the valley of Tayy-Allah ibn Tha'laba in Syria (3), and he led astray the people of that region, and their remnants among them until today say that the ruler is divine, and he removed them from the religion of Islam. So they do not consider the five prayers, nor fasting the month of Ramadan, nor pilgrimage to the Sacred House, nor the prohibition of what Allah and His Messenger have forbidden of carrion, blood, pork, wine, and other things. And these people order (1) the one who responds to them first to adopt Shi'ism and adhere to what the Rafida require and prohibit what they prohibit, then after this they move him step by step until they move him eventually to stripping away from Islam, and that the purpose is the knowledge of their secrets, and it is the knowledge by which the soul is perfected, as the atheist philosophers say. So whoever attains this knowledge reaches the goal, and the acts of worship obligatory upon the common people fall away from him, like the five prayers, fasting Ramadan, and pilgrimage to the House, and what is forbidden becomes permissible for him that is not permissible for others. These people make the Messenger (peace be upon him) if they glorify him and say: He was perfect in knowledge, similar to their atheist leaders, and that he would show to the common people the opposite of what he concealed for the elite. And we have shown the corruption of their statements elsewhere that is not appropriate for this context (2).
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is a critical exposition by Ibn Taymiyya of the Isma'ili sect, particularly the Druze offshoot, and their connection to Greek philosophy, especially Ibn Sina. The author begins by asserting that the stories of these sects are well-known. He then links Ibn Sina and his family to the Isma'ilis during the time of the Fatimid ruler al-Hakim, implying that Ibn Sina's engagement with philosophy stems from this affiliation. The Isma'ilis are described as elevating Muhammad ibn Isma'il to the status of the hidden Imam, claiming he abrogated the Shari'a of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). They hold that their imams are infallible and even superior to prophets, sometimes deifying them. Specifically, al-Hakim sent Nashtakin al-Darazi to the Valley of Tayy-Allah, where he led the people astray, and remnants still believe in al-Hakim's divinity, leading them to abandon the core Islamic practices: the five daily prayers, Ramadan fasting, Hajj, and prohibitions like carrion, blood, pork, and wine. The author explains the gradual initiation process: first, the recruit is instructed in Shi'ism and adopting the Rafida's forbidden/prohibited categories, then advanced step by step until finally shedding Islam altogether. The ultimate goal is 'knowledge of their secrets'—a type of esoteric knowledge that supposedly perfects the soul, a notion attributed to atheist philosophers. Once this knowledge is attained, all religious obligations fall away, and prohibitions become permissible. They liken the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) to their own atheist leaders, claiming he revealed one thing to the elite and another to the common people. Ibn Taymiyya concludes by noting that he has discussed the corruption of their views elsewhere, deeming further elaboration here unnecessary.

Key Terms
الفلاسفة الملاحدة
المستجيب
الإسماعيلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To perfect the soul and thereby make religious obligations unnecessary
B) To gain political power
C) To achieve mystical union with God
D) To interpret the Quran allegorically

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya demonstrates that an elite epistemology that sets aside Shari'a obligations is tantamount to atheism and must be rejected as a corruption of Islam.

Ibn Taymiyya's Reductio Against Esoteric Negation
Ibn Taymiyya refutes esoteric negation of attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's reductio ad absurdum argument against those who claim the Prophet concealed the truth, and identify its logical structure.

Core Idea
Claiming the Prophet hid the truth makes his critics oppose the very Salaf they claim to follow.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya takes on two interrelated errors: the negation of God's attributes (especially al-ʿulūw) and the esoteric claim that the Prophet had a hidden teaching for an elite. He shows that these views lead to a self-defeating contradiction: those who publicize the alleged hidden truth are actually opposing the Prophet and the early Muslims (the Salaf). This lesson will walk through his argumentative strategy step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target groups
Locate the two groups Ibn Taymiyya criticizes: the 'negators of Highness and reported attributes' (al-nufāt lil-ʿulūw wa lil-ṣifāt al-khabariyya) and the esotericists (al-malāḥida) who follow the Batiniyya. Note their beliefs: they reject outward obligations and claim secret knowledge perfects the soul.
The term 'negators' includes those who deny God's attribute of being above His creation, while 'esotericists' use philosophical reasoning to abrogate Islamic law.
2
Extract the esoteric claim about the Prophet
Find where Ibn Taymiyya states that these groups say about the Prophet what they say about their own leaders: that he outwardly taught one thing but inwardly concealed the real truth. This implies the Prophet was not truthful to the common people.
The passage says: 'they make the Prophet ... to be of the same kind as their atheist leaders, and that he used to show the common people the opposite of what he concealed for the elite.'
3
Follow Ibn Taymiyya's reductio
Ibn Taymiyya argues: If the Prophet hid the truth, then those who now publicly display that supposed hidden truth (the negators) are actually opposing the Prophet and his elite companions, who according to them concealed it. The logic is: The Prophet and the Salaf concealed X. The negators now reveal X. Therefore, the negators contradict the Prophet and the Salaf.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum: the opponents' own premise (that the Prophet hid the truth) leads to the conclusion that they themselves are in opposition to the Prophet.
4
Assess the force of the argument
Ibn Taymiyya's argument is strong because it exposes an internal inconsistency: the groups claim to follow the Salaf, yet their actions (publicizing what they claim was hidden) go against the Salaf's practice of accepting the outward teaching. The argument does not rely on external evidence but on the opponents' own assumptions.
The key move is that the Prophet's concealment is taken as a premise; then showing that publicizing that concealed matter violates the Prophet's intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بإلهيّة الحاكم، وقد أخرجهم عن دين الإسلام، فلا يرون الصلوات الخمس، ولا صيام شهر رمضان، ولا حج البيت الحرام، ولا تحريم ما حرَّمه الله ورسوله من الميتة والدم ولحم الخنزير والخمر وغير ذلك. وهؤلاء يأمرون المستجيب لهم أولا إلى التشيع والتزام ما توجبه الرافضة وتحريم ما يحرمونه، ثم بعد هذا ينقلونه درجةً بعد درجة حتى ينقلونه في الآخر إلى الانسلاخ من الإسلام، وأن المقصود هو معرفة أسرارهم، وهو العلم الذي به تكمل النفس، كما تقوله الفلاسفة الملاحدة، فمن حصل له هذا العلم وصل إلى الغاية، وسقطت عنه العبادات التي تجب على العامة، كالصَّلوات الخمس وصيام رمضان وحج البيت، وحلت له المحرمات التي لا تحلّ لغيره. فهؤلاء يجعلون الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا عظموه وقالوا: كان كاملا في العلم = من جنس رؤوسهم الملاحدة، وأنه كان يُظْهِرُ للعامة خلاف ما يبطنه للخاصَّة. وقد بينا من فساد أقوالهم في غير هذا الموضع ما لا يناسبه هذا المقام. فإن المقصود هنا أن هؤلاء النُّفاة للعلو وللصفات الخبرية، كصاحب (المُلْحَة) وأمثاله، يقولون في الرسول من جنس قول هؤلاء، وأن الذي أظهره ليس هو الحقِّ الثابت في نفس الأمر؛ لأن ذلك ما كان يمكنه إظهاره للعامة. فإذا كانوا يقولون هذا في الرسول نفسه، فكيف القولُ في أتباعه من سلف الأمة من الصحابة والتابعين؟! ومن كان هذا أصل قوله في الرسول والسابقين الأولين من المهاجرين والأنصار ، كان مخالفا لهم لا موافقا، لا سيما إذا أظهر النفي الذي كان الرسول وخواص أصحابه عنده يُبْطِئُونَه ولا يُظْهِرُونَه، فإنه يكون مخالفًا لهم أيضًا.
By the divinity of the ruler, and they have taken them out of the religion of Islam, so they do not observe the five prayers, nor fasting the month of Ramadan, nor pilgrimage to the Sacred House, nor prohibition of what Allah and His Messenger have forbidden of carrion, blood, pork, wine, and other things. And these people first command the one who responds to them to adopt Shi'ism and what the Rafida require and to prohibit what they prohibit, then after this they move him degree by degree until they finally move him to stripping himself of Islam, and that the purpose is knowledge of their secrets, which is the knowledge by which the soul is perfected, as the atheist philosophers say. So whoever attains this knowledge reaches the goal, and the acts of worship that are obligatory upon the common people fall away from him, like the five prayers, fasting Ramadan, and pilgrimage to the House, and the forbidden things that are not lawful for others become lawful for him. These people make the Prophet, may Allah bless him and give him peace, when they magnify him and say: he was perfect in knowledge, to be of the same kind as their atheist leaders, and that he used to show the common people the opposite of what he concealed for the elite. And we have shown the corruption of their statements in other places that are not appropriate for this context. For the purpose here is that these negators of the divine attribute of Highness and the attributes reported in scripture, like the author of al-Mulha and his ilk, say concerning the Prophet the same kind of thing as these people say, and that what he showed is not the truth established in the matter itself, because that was not possible for him to show to the common people. If they say this about the Prophet himself, then what about his followers from the early generations of the Ummah, the Companions and the Followers?! Whoever has this as his principle regarding the Prophet and the foremost predecessors among the Emigrants and Helpers, he is opposing them, not agreeing with them, especially if he publicly displays the negation that the Prophet and his elite companions, in his view, concealed and did not show, for then he is also opposing them.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of groups that negate God’s attributes (specifically the attribute of Highness and other reported attributes) and adopt an esoteric interpretation of Islam. The author begins by describing how these groups lead people away from Islam step by step: first they call to Shi'ism, then gradually to the abandonment of Islamic obligations like prayer, fasting, and pilgrimage, and eventually to the justification of forbidden things. They claim that the goal is to obtain secret knowledge, similar to the atheist philosophers. Then Ibn Taymiyya points out that these people also claim that the Prophet had hidden knowledge and that what he publicly taught was not the real truth – a claim that elevates the Prophet to the level of their own heretical leaders. The author then refutes this by arguing that if the Prophet himself is accused of concealing the truth, then how much more would this apply to the Salaf (the early Muslims)? Anyone who holds such a view about the Prophet and the Companions is actually contradicting them, not following them. The passage uses a reductio ad absurdum: if the Prophet and his elite companions hid the truth, then those who now publicize that hidden negation are actually opposing the Prophet and his companions. This passage is a strong critique of theological positions that lead to esotericism and the rejection of clear Islamic teachings.

Key Terms
النُّفاة للعلو وللصفات الخبرية
الملاحدة

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's reductio shows that esoteric negation of God's attributes and claims about the Prophet's hidden teaching are self-defeating because they logically oppose the Prophet and the Salaf.

The A Fortiori Refutation of Deniers of Divine Attributes
Ibn Taymiyya refutes deniers using an a fortiori argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and reconstruct the a fortiori (qiyas al-awlawi) argument used by Ibn Taymiyya to refute those who claim the Prophet concealed the truth of divine attributes.

Core Idea
If accusers claim the Prophet hid the truth, then the Salaf are even more suspect—a devastating a fortiori refutation.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya exposes a fatal internal contradiction in the position of those who deny divine attributes. They claim the Prophet did not reveal the true reality of God's attributes to the common people. Ibn Taymiyya turns this claim against them with a powerful logical tool: the a fortiori argument (qiyas al-awlawi). By understanding this move, you will learn how classical theologians refuted heretical positions without entering into detailed metaphysical debates, focusing instead on self-contradiction and betrayal of the Salaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Accusers' Claim
Find the exact statement that the deniers make about the Prophet. In the passage, the author says they claim 'that what he manifested is not the truth fixed in itself; because that could not be manifested to the common people.' This means they accuse the Prophet of deliberately concealing the true reality of divine attributes from the masses.
2
Extract the Author's A Fortiori Move
Observe how Ibn Taymiyya extends the accusation from the Prophet to the Salaf: 'So if they say this about the Messenger himself, then what about his followers from the predecessors of the nation, the Companions and the Successors?!' This is a classic a fortiori argument: if the more authoritative figure (the Prophet) is accused of concealment, then those who follow him (the Salaf) are even more deserving of that accusation.
The logical structure: If P then Q; P (accusation against the Prophet) is asserted; therefore Q (accusation against the Salaf) necessarily follows, but the deniers claim to follow the Salaf, hence contradiction.
3
Assess the Force of the Argument
Why is this argument devastating? The deniers claim to be followers of the Salaf. But if the Salaf also concealed the truth (as the logic forces), then the deniers' own position is undermined: they cannot both revere the Salaf and accuse them of concealment. The argument shows internal inconsistency in the deniers' stance.
4
Recognize the Fallacy in the Deniers' Position
The deniers implicitly admit that the true understanding was hidden from the majority. But the Prophet and the Salaf were tasked with conveying the message clearly. Thus, the deniers' claim contradicts the fundamental trustworthiness of the prophetic message and the Salaf's transmission. Ibn Taymiyya concludes that whoever holds this view is actually opposing the Salaf, not following them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن المقصود هنا أن هؤلاء النُّفاة للعلو وللصفات الخبرية، كصاحب (المُلْحَة) وأمثاله، يقولون في الرسول من جنس قول هؤلاء، وأن الذي أظهره ليس هو الحق الثابت في نفس الأمر؛ لأن ذلك ما كان يمكنه إظهاره للعامة. فإذا كانوا يقولون هذا في الرسول نفسه، فكيف القول في أتباعه من سلف الأمة من الصحابة والتابعين؟! ومن كان هذا أصل قوله في الرسول والسابقين الأولين من المهاجرين والأنصار، كان مخالفا لهم لا موافقا، لا سيما إذا أظهر النفي الذي كان الرسول وخواص أصحابه عنده يُبْطِئُونَه ولا يُظْهِرُونَه، فإنه يكون مخالفًا لهم أيضًا. وهذا المسلك يراه عامة النفاة، كابن رشد الحفيد وغيره، وفي كلام أبي حامد من هذا قطعة كبيرة. وابن عقيل وأمثاله قد يقولون أحيانًا هذا، لكن ابن عقيل الغالب عليه إذا خرج عن السنة أن يميل إلى التجهم والاعتزال في أول أمره، بخلاف آخر ما كان عليه فقد خرج إلى السنة المحضة. وأبو حامد يميل إلى الفلسفة لكنه أظهرها في قالب التصوف والعبارات الإسلامية؛ ولهذا رد عليه علماء المسلمين، حتى أخص أصحابه أبو بكر بن قال: «شيخنا أبو حامد دخل في بطن الفلاسفة، ثم أراد أن يخرج فما قدر»، وقد حكى عنه من القول بمذاهب الباطنية ما يوجد تصديق ذلك في كتبه، ورد عليه العلماء المذكورون قبل.
For the intent here is that these deniers of the attribute of being above and of the reported attributes, like the author of al-Mulha and his ilk, say about the Messenger a kind of saying of these people, and that what he manifested is not the truth fixed in itself; because that could not be manifested to the common people. So if they say this about the Messenger himself, then what about his followers from the predecessors of the nation, the Companions and the Successors?! Whoever has this as the basis of his statement concerning the Messenger and the first forerunners among the Emigrants and Helpers, he is opposing them, not agreeing, especially if he manifests the negation which the Messenger and his special companions used to conceal and not manifest, then he is also opposing them. This path is seen by the generality of the deniers, like Ibn Rushd the grandson and others, and in the speech of Abu Hamid there is a large portion of this. Ibn Aqil and his likes sometimes say this, but Ibn Aqil, when he deviates from the Sunnah, mostly inclines to tajsim and i'tizal at the beginning of his affair, unlike his latter state when he came out to the pure Sunnah. And Abu Hamid inclines to philosophy but he manifests it in the mold of Sufism and Islamic expressions; therefore the Muslim scholars refuted him, even his most special companions, Abu Bakr ibn said: 'Our teacher Abu Hamid entered into the belly of the philosophers, then wanted to come out but could not.' And it has been narrated from him about the saying of the doctrines of the Batinites what confirms that is found in his books, and he was refuted by the aforementioned scholars before.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is a critique of a specific group of theologians: those who deny God's attribute of being above (al-‘uluw) and the reported attributes (al-sifat al-khabariyya), exemplified by the author of al-Mulha. The author argues that these deniers claim the Prophet Muhammad did not reveal the true reality of these attributes to the common people, implying that the Prophet's public teachings were not the absolute truth. The author finds this assertion extremely problematic, reasoning that if they say this about the Prophet himself, then their view of the Prophet's Companions and the early generations (Salaf) is even worse. Consequently, anyone who holds such a view is actually opposing the Prophet and the Salaf, not following them. The author then identifies that this path is common among deniers, mentioning Ibn Rushd (Averroes) and noting that Abu Hamid al-Ghazali's works contain a large portion of this deviant idea. The discussion moves to Ibn Aqil, who sometimes expressed such views but later repented to the pure Sunnah. The author criticizes al-Ghazali for mixing philosophy with Sufism and Islamic terminology, which led to refutation from Muslim scholars. He cites a statement from al-Ghazali's close companion Abu Bakr ibn al-‘Arabi (the name is incomplete in the text) that al-Ghazali entered philosophy and could not exit. The passage ends by noting that al-Ghazali was also accused of Batinite (esoteric) doctrines, and the earlier mentioned scholars refuted him. This is a classic Ibn Taymiyyan critique of theological deviation, emphasizing that the Salaf were not concealers of truth but manifesters of it.

العلو
الصفات الخبرية
السلف

The a fortiori critique shows that if the Prophet is accused of concealment, the Salaf are even more implicated, refuting the deniers' claim to follow them.
