Divine Names: The 'Limbs' vs 'Accidents' Argument
Author compares two refusals regarding divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's argument that refraining from calling divine attributes 'limbs' is more justified than refusing to call them 'accidents', and explain why.

Core Idea
Divine names are revealed, not invented; calling attributes 'limbs' implies imperfection, while 'accidents' is a broader category.

This passage from Ibn Taymiyya's critique tackles a key theological distinction: how we name divine attributes. The author sets up a comparison between two positions—one that refrains from using the term 'limbs' (jewarih) for God's attributes, and another that refuses to call them 'accidents' (a'rad). The aim is to show that the former is more reasonable, given the implications of the word 'limbs' and the revealed nature of divine names.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle of Divine Names
Notice that the author begins by stating a foundational principle: divine names and attributes are based on revelation (sam'iyya), not on mere opinion. This frames the entire argument.
This principle is shared by the Ash'ari school and Ibn Taymiyya.
2
Distinguish the Two Positions
The author compares two groups: those who refrain from calling divine attributes 'jewarih' (limbs) and those who refuse to call them 'a'rad' (accidents). Which group does he consider more excusable, and why?
The first group refrains from a specific term; the second rejects a broader category.
3
Analyze the Reasoning for 'jewarih'
The author explains that human attributes include both accidents (like knowledge) and bodies (like face and hand). Calling the latter 'limbs' is more specific and carries connotations of acquisition, benefit, and divisibility—concepts inappropriate for God.
Thus, refraining from 'jewarih' avoids implying imperfection.
4
Note the Consensus of the Salaf
The author adds a fourth point: the affirmation of these attributes (face, hand) is agreed upon by the early generations and major theological schools, including the Kullabiyya, Karamiyya, and Ash'ariyya. This shows that the objection is not unique to his own position.
This strengthens the argument by citing authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضًا، فأسماء الله وأسماء صفاته عندهم شرعية سمعية لا تطلق بمجرد الرأي، فهم في الامتناع من هذه الأسماء أحق بالعذر ممن امتنع من تسمية صفاته أعراضا، وذلك أن الصفات التي لنا منها ما هو عرض كالعلم والقدرة، ومنها ما هو جسم وجوهر قائم بنفسه كالوجه واليد، وتسمية هذه جوارح وأعضاء أخص من تسميتها أجساما؛ لما في ذلك من معنى الاكتساب والانتفاع والتصرف وجواز التفريق والبعضية. الوجه الرابع: أن هذا السؤال لا يختص بهؤلاء، بل إثبات جنس هذه الصفات قد اتفق عليه سلف الأمة وأئمتها من أهل الفقه والحديث والتصوف والمعرفة، وأئمة أهل الكلام من الكلابية والكرامية والأشعرية، كل هؤلاء يثبتون الله صفة الوجه واليد ونحو ذلك.
Also, the names of God and the names of His attributes according to them are based on revelation and hearing, not given by mere opinion. So they, in refraining from these names, are more deserving of excuse than those who refrained from calling His attributes accidents. That is because the attributes that we have include what is an accident, like knowledge and power, and include what is a body and a self-subsistent substance, like the face and hand. Naming these as limbs and organs is more specific than naming them as bodies, due to the meaning of acquisition, benefit, disposal, and possibility of division and partiality. The fourth aspect: this question is not specific to these people, but the affirmation of the genus of these attributes has been agreed upon by the predecessors of the nation and its imams from the people of jurisprudence, hadith, Sufism, and knowledge, and the imams of the theologians from the Kullabiyya, Karamiyya, and Ash'ariyya—all of these affirm for God the attribute of the face and hand and so forth.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage defends the position of those who affirm divine attributes like face and hand but refrain from calling them 'limbs' (jewarih). The author argues that divine names are based on revelation, not arbitrary opinion. Those who refuse to call these attributes 'limbs' are more excusable than those who refuse to call them 'accidents' (a'rad). The reasoning is that human attributes include both accidents (like knowledge) and bodies (like face and hand). Calling them 'limbs' is more specific than calling them 'bodies' because 'limbs' imply acquisition, benefit, etc.—terms that in ordinary use imply composition and imperfection. The 'fourth aspect' then points out that this issue is not unique to the Hanbalites; many schools (Kullabiyya, Karamiyya, Ash'ariyya) affirm these attributes. The argument is essentially that the opponents' objection is weak because the precedent of the salaf and major scholars supports affirmation.

Key Terms
جوارح
أعراض
سمعية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why are those who refrain from calling divine attributes 'jewarih' more excusable than those who refuse to call them 'a'rad'?
A) Because 'jewarih' is a term of praise
B) Because human attributes include both brains and bodies
C) Because some human attributes are accidents and some are bodies; calling attributes 'limbs' is more specific and implies imperfection
D) Because the Qur'an explicitly forbids the term 'jewarih'

Key Takeaway
Divine names are established by revelation; comparisons to human attributes must be carefully qualified to avoid implying imperfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the attribute 'al-yad' (hand of God). Using the author's reasoning, explain why it is more appropriate to affirm the attribute but refrain from calling it a 'limb' (jarih).
?
Identify another divine attribute (e.g., 'al-wajh' face) and apply the same distinction: affirm it as revealed, but avoid terms that imply imperfection. Write a one-paragraph defense of this approach.

The Universality of Affirmation and Negation
Author argues against the exclusivity of affirming divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's inductive argument against the exclusivity of affirming divine attributes and identify the logical structure of his enumeration.

Core Idea
The affirmation of attributes is not a monopoly of any one sect—it is found across all groups, even among non-Muslims.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya takes on a claim that some groups (particularly Hanbalis) hold a unique position regarding divine attributes. He uses an inductive argument, enumerating various groups to show that both affirmation and negation are universal. This lesson breaks down his method and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target claim
What claim is Ibn Taymiyya refuting? That any single group, such as the Hanbalis, owns the position of affirming divine attributes. He aims to show that no group has exclusivity.
The claim is implicit in the accusation that only Hanbalis affirm attributes literally.
2
Extract the enumeration
List the groups he mentions: Ahl al-Sunnah, Hanbalis, Sufis, Malikis, Shafi'is, Hanafis, then Shi'a, Jews, Christians, Sabians, and philosophers. He includes both Muslim and non-Muslim groups.
This is an inductive survey; he does not claim completeness.
3
Observe the pattern
In each group, both affirmers and negators exist. He notes that some non-Muslim affirmers even affirm more than some Muslim theologians. This refutes the idea of exclusivity.
The pattern is that no group is purely one position; both poles are present.
4
Note the qualifying statement
He adds that affirmation is more prevalent among followers of the messengers, and negation more prevalent among non-followers. This refinement maintains the truth of the universal distribution while acknowledging a general tendency.
This prevents overgeneralization while preserving the core argument.
5
Assess the conclusion
The conclusion is that no group has an exclusive claim to affirmation. The Salafi position is not a partisan innovation but a continuation of the prophetic tradition available to all.
This challenges sectarian claims and opens theological methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحديث جملة ما عليه أهلُ السُّنة وأصحاب الحديث: الإقرار بكذا وكذا ، وأن الله على عرشه أستوى، وأن له يدين بلا كيف، كما قال: ﴿خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَى﴾، وكما قال : ﴿بَلْ يَدَاهُ مَبْسُوطَتَانِ﴾، وأن له عينين بلا كيف، كما قال : ﴿تَجْرِى بِأَعْيُنِنَا﴾، وأن له وجها، كما قال: ﴿وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الْجَلَلِ وَالْإِكْرَامِ﴾.

وقد قدمنا فيما تقدم أن جميع أئمة الطوائف هم من أهل الإثبات وما من شيء ذكره أبو الفرج وغيره مما هو موجود في الحنبلية ــ سواء كان الصوابُ فيه مع المثبت، أو مع النافي، أو كان فيه تفصيل - إلا وذلك موجود فيما شاء الله من أهل الحديث والصُّوفية والمالكية والشافعية والحنفية ونحوهم، بل هو موجود في الطوائف التي لا تنتحل السنة والجماعة والحديث ولا مذهبَ السَّلف، مثل الشيعة وغيرهم، ففيهم في طرفي الإثبات والنفي ما لا يوجد في هذه الطوائف.

وكذلك في أهل الكتابين - أهل التوراة والإنجيل - توجد هذه المذاهب المتقابلة في النفي والإثبات، وكذلك الصَّابئة من الفلاسفة وغيرهم لهم تقابل في النفي والإثبات، حتى إن منهم من يُثْبِتُ ما لا يُثْبِتُه كثير من متكلّمة الصفاتية، ولكن جنس الإثبات على المتّبعين للرسل أغلب من الذين آمنوا واليهود والنصارى والصابئة المهتدين، وجنس النفي على غير المتبعين للرُّسل أغلب من المشركين والصابئة المبتدعة.

وقد ذكرنا في غير هذا الجواب مذهب سلف الأمة وأئمتها بألفاظها وألفاظ من نقل ذلك من جميع الطوائف، بحيث لا يبقى لأحد من الطوائف اختصاص بالإثبات.

ومن ذلك ما ذكره شيخُ الحرمين أبو الحسن [ محمد بن عبد الملك الكَرَجِي، في كتابه الذي سماه الفصول في الأصول عن الأئمة الفحول إلزاما لذوي البدع والفُضول» ، وكان من أئمة الشَّافعية، ذكر فيـه مـن كـلام
The statement (al-hadith) is the sum of what the people of the Sunnah and the companions of hadith are upon: affirming such-and-such, and that Allah is above His Throne, and that He has two hands without modality, as He said: 'I created with My two hands,' and as He said: 'Nay, both His hands are outstretched,' and that He has two eyes without modality, as He said: 'Sailing under Our eyes,' and that He has a face, as He said: 'And there will remain the Face of your Lord, Owner of Majesty and Honor.'

And we have previously mentioned that all the leaders of the sects are among the people of affirmation (ahl al-ithbat), and there is nothing that Abu al-Faraj and others mentioned that is present among the Hanbalis — whether the truth in it is with the affirmer, or with the negator, or whether there is detail — except that it is present, by the will of Allah, among the people of hadith, Sufis, Malikis, Shafi'is, Hanafis, and the like. Rather, it is present among the sects that do not adopt the Sunnah, the community, the hadith, or the way of the Salaf, such as the Shi'a and others. Among them, in both extremes of affirmation and negation, there is what is not found in these sects.

Similarly, among the People of the Two Books — the people of the Torah and the Gospel — these opposing doctrines in negation and affirmation exist, and likewise the Sabians, the philosophers, and others have opposition in negation and affirmation, to the point that among them are some who affirm what many theologians of the attributists (sifatiyya) do not affirm. But the genus of affirmation is more prevalent among the followers of the messengers than among those who believed, the Jews, Christians, and guided Sabians, and the genus of negation is more prevalent among those who do not follow the messengers than among the polytheists and heretical Sabians.

And we have mentioned elsewhere in this response the doctrine of the Salaf of the community and their imams, with their own words and the words of those who transmitted that from all the sects, such that no one among the sects retains any exclusivity in affirmation.

And among that is what the Shaykh of the Two Sanctuaries, Abu al-Hasan Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Karaji, mentioned in his book entitled 'The Chapters on the Fundamentals from the Eminent Imams, as a Binding Proof against the People of Innovation and Excess', and he was among the Shafi'i imams. He mentioned in it from the speech...
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is an inductive argument by enumeration. The author aims to refute the claim that the position of affirming divine attributes (al-ithbat) is exclusive to the Hanbalis or any single sect. He begins by stating the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah: affirming God's attributes (hands, eyes, face) without modality (bila kayf). Then he argues that all sects have both affirmers and negators — not only the Hanbalis and other Sunni groups (Sufis, Malikis, Shafi'is, Hanafis) but even those outside the Sunni fold (Shi'a), and even among Jews, Christians, and Sabians (including philosophers). Some non-Muslims affirm more attributes than some Muslim theologians. However, the author clarifies that affirmation predominates among followers of the messengers, while negation predominates among those who reject them. He concludes by stating that no group has exclusive right to claim affirmation, and he cites al-Karaji's book as an example of a Shafi'i scholar compiling the Salafi creed. The argument uses enumeration of groups to demonstrate the universality of both positions.

Key Terms
الإثبات
النفي
أهل السنة والجماعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which group has an exclusive claim to affirming God's attributes?
A) The Hanbalis only
B) The Shafi'is only
C) All groups have both affirmers and negators, so no group is exclusive
D) Only the Salaf

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's inductive argument demonstrates that theological positions are not the exclusive property of any single sect, and that a proper methodology looks at the evidence across groups.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Using Ibn Taymiyya's method, identify at least three modern Islamic groups (e.g., Salafis, Ash'aris, Sufis) and find examples of both affirmation and negation of attributes within each group. 2. Write a short critique of the statement 'Affirming God's hands is only a Hanbali position' using Ibn Taymiyya's inductive approach — enumerate groups and show coexistence of both positions.

Third Argument: Madhhab and 'Aqida Consistency
Author presents third argument against madhhab-'aqida separation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the third argument against separating madhhab and 'aqida and evaluate its validity.

Core Idea
Following a madhhab necessitates accepting its founder’s creed.

This passage presents a third argument: a binding proof that forces consistency between one's madhhab and 'aqida. The author argues that the imams themselves condemned their doctrinal opponents, so claiming to follow them while diverging in creed is a logical and religious contradiction. He illustrates with examples: Shafi'i-Ash'ari, Hanbali-Mu'tazili, and Malikis adopting Ash'arism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
Locate the position the author is attacking: the separation of madhhab (school of jurisprudence) and 'aqida (creed). Many people claim to follow an imam in fiqh but hold a different creed.
The author calls this 'intihal' (adoption) of a madhhab while opposing the imam in creed.
2
Extract the imams' historical positions
Find in the passage how al-Shafi'i, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, and Malik treated opposing sects like Jahmiyya, Mu'tazila, etc. They declared them misguided (tadlil), innovators (tabdi'), or disbelievers (takfir).
These condemnations are the basis for the binding argument.
3
Recognize the logical contradiction
Understand why the author says it is contradictory: if Imam X declared group Y deviant, then claiming to follow X while adhering to Y's beliefs is inconsistent. The author calls it 'didd' (contradiction) and even 'irtidad' (apostasy) in the Shafi'i-Ash'ari case.
The contradiction is between the claimed allegiance and the actual creedal content.
4
Assess the argument's strength
Evaluate whether the argument holds. Consider if the imam's condemnations are definitive and whether later developments (e.g., Ash'arism as a synthesis) can be reconciled. The author assumes the imam's creed is fixed and incompatible with the opposing school.
This step requires critical thinking about historical context and doctrinal evolution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: ووجه ثالث لا بدَّ مِن أن نبين فيه، فنقول: إن في النقل عن هؤلاء إلزاما للحجة على كل من ينتحل مذهب إمام يخالفه في العقيدة، فإن أحدهما لا محالة يضلل صاحبه أو يبدعُه أو يكفرُه، فانتحال مذهبه مع مخالفته في العقيدة مستنكر والله شرعًا وطبعا.
فمن قال: أنا شافعي الشَّرع أشعري الاعتقاد، قلنا له: هذا من الأضداد، لا بل من الارتداد؛ إذ لم يكن الشافعي أشعري الاعتقاد. ومن قال: أنا حنبلي في الفروع، معتز لي في الأصول، قلنا: قد ضللت إذا عن سواء السبيل فيما تزعمه؛ إذ لم يكن أحمد معتز لي الدين والاجتهاد.
قال: وقد أفتتن أيضًا خلق من المالكية بمذاهب الأشعرية، وهذه والله شينةٌ وعار، وفلتةٌ تعود بالوبال والنكال وسوء الدار، على منتحل مذاهب هؤلاء الأئمة الكبار، فإن مذهبهم ما رويناه من تكفيرهم الجهمية والمعتزلة والقدرية والواقفية وتكفيرهم اللفظية.
He said: And a third aspect that we must clarify: we say that in reporting from these (imams) there is a binding argument against everyone who adopts the madhhab of an imam while opposing him in creed. For one of them inevitably declares the other misguided, an innovator, or a disbeliever. So adopting his madhhab while opposing him in creed is objectionable by the Shari'a and by nature. 
Thus whoever says: 'I am Shafi'i in Shari'a, Ash'ari in creed,' we say to him: This is a contradiction, nay rather apostasy, for al-Shafi'i was not Ash'ari in creed. And whoever says: 'I am Hanbali in furu', Mu'tazili in usul,' we say: You have strayed from the straight path in what you claim, for Ahmad was not Mu'tazili in religion and ijtihad. 
He said: Indeed many of the Malikis have also become infatuated with the doctrines of the Ash'aris. This, by Allah, is a disgrace and shame, a blunder that will bring ruin, punishment, and evil abode upon those who adopt the madhhabs of these great imams, for their madhhab is what we have transmitted of their declaring the Jahmiyya, Mu'tazila, Qadariyya, Waqifiyya, and the Lafziyya as disbelievers.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a critical argument against the separation of madhhab (school of jurisprudence) and 'aqida (creed). The author presents a third point: following an imam such as al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, or Malik requires adopting his creedal positions as well. The reasoning is that these imams themselves declared their opponents (e.g., Jahmiyya, Mu'tazila) to be misguided or disbelievers. Hence, claiming to follow them while adhering to a contradictory creed (e.g., Ash'ari, Mu'tazili) is logically and religiously inconsistent. The author calls such claims 'contradiction' and even 'apostasy' in the case of al-Shafi'i. He also criticizes Malikis who adopted Ash'ari doctrines, recalling that Malik's school historically opposed those groups. This is a polemical refutation of those who attempt to compartmentalize their religious identity.

Key Terms
إلزام الحجة
انتحال
ضلل
بدع
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the consequence for someone who claims 'I am Shafi'i in Shari'a but Ash'ari in creed'?
A) It is permissible because fiqh and creed are independent.
B) It is a contradiction (didd) and even apostasy (irtidad).
C) It is acceptable as long as he performs the rituals.
D) It is a minor sin that can be overlooked.

Key Takeaway
The third argument shows that adopting a madhhab requires accepting its founder's creedal positions, as the imams themselves condemned opposing views.

Subsumption of Minority Opinions: A Dialectical Defense
Author defends his selection of scholars by explaining how other scholars' views are subsumed under the major imams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze a jadal exchange by identifying the objection, the author's response using indiraj, and evaluating the sufficiency of the evidence.

Core Idea
Subsumption (indiraj) justifies selective citation: minority opinions are absorbed by major schools.

This passage from a work of legal methodology presents a dialectical exchange: an objector questions why the author only cites four major imams. The author's reply introduces the concept of indiraj (subsumption) to explain that other scholars' views are effectively contained within these major schools. In this lesson, we will dissect this argument step by step, learning how jadal works and how subsumption functions as a historical-legal principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Find the objector's question in the passage. What is the challenge? The objector asks why the author restricts transmission to only four imams (al-Shafi'i, Malik, al-Thawri, Ahmad) and ignores others like al-Awza'i and al-Layth.
2
Extract the author's main response
The author responds that the other scholars' schools have been subsumed (indiraj) under the major schools. Find the key phrase 'أندرجت مذاهبهم' and note the general claim.
3
Analyze the evidence for each example
The author gives specific cases: Ibn 'Uyaynah's school subsumed under al-Shafi'i and Ahmad because his students wrote his rulings; al-Layth's opinions agree with Malik and al-Thawri; al-Awza'i's opinions align with one of three major imams; Ishaq agrees with Ahmad. For each, trace the reasoning.
Notice how the evidence varies: some by student transmission, some by doctrinal agreement.
4
Evaluate the source and conclusion
The author cites al-Isfarayini's 'Ta'liqah' as his source. Then he adds that Abu Zur'ah and Abu Hatim's choices are subsumed under Ahmad, and al-Bukhari left no independent choice. Assess whether the author has sufficiently answered the objection, and whether subsumption is a valid methodological principle.
Think about potential counterarguments: Is agreement always complete? Does subsumption imply the minority views are fully represented?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبسَط الكلامَ في مسألة اللفظ إلى أن قال: فأما غير من ذكرناه من الأئمة فلم ينتحل أحدٌ مذهبهم ، فلذلك لم نتعرّض للنقل عنهم.
قال: فإن قيل: فهلا أقتصرتم إذا على النقل عمَّن شاع مذهبه وانتُحِلَ اختياره من أصحاب الحديث، وهم الأئمة: الشافعي ومالك والثوري وأحمد، إذ لا نرى أحدا ينتحل مذهب الأوزاعي والليث وسائرهم؟
قلنا: لأن من ذكرناه من الأئمة سوى هؤلاء أرباب المذاهب في الجملة، إذ كانوا قدوةً في عصرهم، ثم أندرجت مذاهبهم بالآخرة (۱) تحت مذاهب الأئمة المعتبرة.
وذلك أن ابن عيينة كان قدوة، ولكن لم يصنف في الذي كان يختاره من الأحكام، وإنما صنف أصحابه، وهم الشافعي وأحمد وإسحاق، فاندرج مذهبه تحت مذاهبهما (۲) . وأما الليث بن سعد، فلم يقم أصحابه بمذهبه، قال الشافعي: «لم يُرْزَق الأصحابَ» (۳) ، إلا أن قوله يوافق قول مالك أو قول الثوري لا يخطئهما،
فاندرج مذهبه تحت مذهبهما.
وأما الأوزاعي، فلا نرى له فى أعم المسائل قولا إلا ويوافق قول مالك أو قول الثوري أو قول الشافعي، فاندرج أختياره أيضًا تحت أختيار هؤلاء.
وكذلك أختيار إسحاق يندرج تحت مذهب أحمد؛ لتوافقهما. قال: فإن قيل : فمن أين وقعت على هذا التفصيل والبيان في أندراج مذاهب هؤلاء تحت مذاهب الأئمة؟
قلت: من «التعليقة» للشيخ أبي حامد الإسفراييني(۱)، التي هي ديوان الشرائع، وأم البدائع في بيان الأحكام، ومذاهب العلماء الأعلام، وأصول الحُجَج العظام، في المختلف والمؤتلف (۲).
قال: وأما أختيار أبي زرعة وأبي حاتم في الصَّلاة والأحكام - مما قرأته وسمعته من مجموعيهما ـ فهو موافق لقول أحمد ومندرج تحته، وذلك مشهور.
وأما البخاري فلم أر له أختيارًا، ولكن سمعت محمد بن طاهر
And he expanded the discussion on the issue of wording until he said: As for those other than the imams we mentioned, no one adopted their school, therefore we did not bother to transmit from them. He said: If it is said: Why then did you restrict yourselves to transmitting from those whose school became widespread and whose choice was adopted among the hadith scholars—namely the imams al-Shafi'i, Malik, al-Thawri, and Ahmad—since we see no one adopting the school of al-Awza'i, al-Layth, and the rest? We said: Because the imams we mentioned besides these are masters of schools in general, for they were leaders in their time; then their schools were eventually subsumed under the schools of the respected imams. This is because Ibn 'Uyaynah was a leader, but he did not author [works] on the rulings he chose; rather his students—al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and Ishaq—authored, so his school was subsumed under their two schools. As for al-Layth ibn Sa'd, his students did not uphold his school; al-Shafi'i said: 'He was not granted students,' except that his opinion agrees with the opinion of Malik or the opinion of al-Thawri and does not deviate from them, so his school was subsumed under their two schools. As for al-Awza'i, we do not see him in the most general issues having an opinion except that it agrees with the opinion of Malik, or the opinion of al-Thawri, or the opinion of al-Shafi'i, so his choice was also subsumed under the choice of these. Likewise, the choice of Ishaq is subsumed under the school of Ahmad due to their agreement. He said: If it is said: From where did you come upon this detail and clarification regarding the subsumption of the schools of these under the schools of the imams? I said: From the 'Ta'liqah' of Shaykh Abu Hamid al-Isfarayini, which is the diwan of laws, the mother of novelties in explaining rulings, the schools of eminent scholars, and the foundations of great proofs, in what is different and what is agreed upon. He said: As for the choice of Abu Zur'ah and Abu Hatim regarding prayer and rulings—from what I read and heard from their collections—it agrees with the saying of Ahmad and is subsumed under it, and that is well-known. As for al-Bukhari, I did not see for him a choice, but I heard Muhammad ibn Tahir...
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical exchange (jadal) where the author defends his methodology of only transmitting from the major imams (al-Shafi'i, Malik, al-Thawri, Ahmad). The objector asks why they ignore scholars like al-Awza'i and al-Layth. The answer is that the views of those other scholars have been subsumed (indiraj) under the major schools. The author gives concrete examples: Ibn 'Uyaynah's school is subsumed under al-Shafi'i and Ahmad because his students were those imams; al-Layth's opinions agree with Malik and al-Thawri; al-Awza'i's opinions agree with one of the three major imams; Ishaq's opinions agree with Ahmad. The objector then asks for the source of this detailed classification, and the author points to al-Isfarayini's 'Ta'liqah', a major work that synthesizes and compares rulings. Finally, the author mentions that the choices of Abu Zur'ah and Abu Hatim agree with Ahmad, and that al-Bukhari left no independent choice. This argument shows the author's care in justifying his selection of authorities based on historical and doctrinal subsumption, a key concern in Islamic legal methodology.

Key Terms
اندراج (indiraj): The subsumption or absorption of a minor school's opinions under the broader, more widely accepted school of a major imam. [Note: This term is used here in a historical-legal sense; in logic it can mean inclusion of a term under a genus.]
مذهب (madhhab): A school of thought, particularly the juristic school of an imam like al-Shafi'i or Malik. [Note: In Islamic jurisprudence, madhhab is standard; in logic it can mean opinion or doctrine.]
اختيار (ikhtiyar): The preferred legal opinion of a scholar, distinct from the established school doctrine. [Note: This term is used in usul al-fiqh for juristic preference; in logic it means free choice.]
تعليقة (ta'liqah): A supercommentary or gloss; here specifically referring to al-Isfarayini's work that synthesizes legal rulings and schools. [Note: In later usage, ta'liqah often denotes a gloss on a commentary; here it is an independent work of comparative fiqh.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the author not transmit from al-Awza'i and al-Layth?
A) Because their books were lost and inaccessible.
B) Because their opinions are always in agreement with one of the major imams (Malik, al-Thawri, or al-Shafi'i) and thus subsumed under their schools.
C) Because they were not considered reliable hadith scholars.
D) Because the author only transmits from those who have a large number of followers.

Key Takeaway
Subsumption (indiraj) is a powerful methodological tool: the views of lesser-known scholars are absorbed into major schools, so citing the major imams suffices.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find another example in Islamic legal literature where a scholar justifies selective citation using subsumption or similar reasoning. Identify the objection and response structure.
?
Construct a jadal exchange: as an objector, challenge a scholar's selection of sources in a hypothetical fiqh issue; as the scholar, respond using the concept of indiraj.

Salafi Creed: Quran Uncreated & Attributes Affirmed
Author cites early authorities affirming the Quran as uncreated speech and Allah's attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key Salafi authorities and their statements affirming the Quran as uncreated speech and Allah's literal attributes.

Core Idea
The Quran is Allah's uncreated speech; His attributes are real, not metaphorical.

This passage from Ibn Taymiyya's Naqd al-Mantiq cements the Salafi creed by citing early authorities. These citations are weapons against the logicians who deny or allegorize divine attributes. Understanding them equips you to recognize the foundational evidence for the orthodox position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Authorities
List the four main figures cited in the passage: Ibn Umar, Aisha, Ibn al-Mubarak, Ahmad, Bukhari, and Shafi'i. Note that each provides a distinct aspect of the creed.
These are early Salaf whose statements carry authoritative weight in theological debate.
2
Extract the Core Creedal Claims
For each authority, write down the specific claim about the Quran (e.g., uncreated, every letter uncreated) or about Allah's attributes (e.g., hands, face, laughter).
Focus on the exact wording: 'non makhlooq', 'yad', 'wajh', etc.
3
Find the Proofs
Identify the Quranic verses and hadith cited as evidence for each attribute. For example, verse 5:64 for hands, 39:67 for right hand, 28:88 for face.
These proofs are the scriptural foundation for the Salafi position.
4
Synthesize the Position
Summarize the overall Salafi stance: the Quran is uncreated in all aspects (letters, recitation, written form), and Allah's attributes are affirmed literally without ta'wil or ta'til.
This synthesis is the key takeaway for distinguishing Salafi creed from other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال ابن عمر: خلق الله بيديه أربعة أشياء: آدم، والعرش، والقلم، وجنة عدن، وقال لسائر الخلق كن، فكان. وأنه يتكلم بالوحي كيف يشاء. قالت عائشة رضي الله عنها: لشأني في نفسي كان أحقر من أن يتكلم الله في بوحي يتلى. وأن القرآن كلام الله بجميع جهاته، منزل غير مخلوق، ولا حرف منه مخلوق، منه بدأ وإليه يعود. قال عبد الله بن المبارك: من كفر بحرف من القرآن فقد كفر، ومن قال: لا أؤمن بهذه اللام فقد كفر. وأن الكتب المنزلة على الرسل مئة وأربعة كتب كلام الله غير مخلوق. قال أحمد: وما في اللوح المحفوظ، وما في المصاحف وتلاوة الناس، وكيفما يقرأ، وكيفما يوصف، فهو كلام الله غير مخلوق. قال البخاري: وأقول: في المصحف قرآن، وفي صدور الرجال قرآن، فمن قال غير هذا يستتاب، فإن تاب وإلا فسبيله سبيل الكفر. قال: وذكر الشافعي المعتقد بالدلائل، فقال: الله تعالى أسماء وصفات جاء بها كتابه، وأخبر بها نبيه أمته، لا يسع أحدا من خلق الله قامت عليه الحجة ردها. إلى أن قال: نحو إخبار الله سبحانه إيانا أنه سميع بصير، وأن له يدين بقوله: بَلْ يَدَاهُ مَبْسُوطَتَانِ، وأن له يمينا بقوله: وَالسَّمَاوَاتُ مَطْوِيَّاتٌ بِيَمِينِهِ، وأن له وجها بقوله: كُلُّ شَيْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُ، وقوله: وَيَبْقَى وَجْهُ رَبِّكَ ذُو الْجَلَالِ وَالْإِكْرَامِ، وأن له قدما لقوله: حتى يضع الرب فيه قدمه يعني: جهنم، وأنه يضحك من عبده المؤمن لقوله للذي قتل في سبيل الله: إنه لقي الله وهو يضحك إليه، وأنه يهبط كل ليلة إلى سماء الدنيا لخبر رسول الله بذلك، وأنه ليس بأعور لقول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذ ذكر الدجال فقال: إنه
And Ibn Umar said: Allah created with His two hands four things: Adam, the Throne, the Pen, and the Garden of Eden, and He said to the rest of creation 'Be', and it was. And He speaks through revelation as He wills. Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, said: 'My affair in my own eyes was more insignificant than that Allah should speak about me in a revelation that is recited.' And that the Quran is the speech of Allah in all its aspects, revealed, uncreated, and not a letter of it is created, from Him it began and to Him it returns. Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak said: Whoever disbelieves in a letter of the Quran has disbelieved, and whoever says 'I do not believe in this lam' has disbelieved. And that the books revealed to the messengers are one hundred and four books, the speech of Allah, uncreated. Ahmad said: And what is in the Preserved Tablet, and what is in the mus-hafs and the recitation of people, and however it is recited, and however it is described, it is the speech of Allah, uncreated. Al-Bukhari said: And I say: In the mus-haf is Quran, and in the breasts of men is Quran, so whoever says other than this is asked to repent, and if he repents (it is accepted), otherwise his fate is the fate of disbelief. He said: And al-Shafi'i mentioned the creed based on evidences, and said: Allah has names and attributes that His book has brought, and His Prophet has informed his nation; it is not permissible for anyone of Allah's creation against whom the proof is established to reject them. Until he said: Such as Allah's informing us that He is Hearing, Seeing, and that He has two hands by His saying: 'Nay, both His hands are outstretched' (Al-Ma'idah 5:64), and that He has a right hand by His saying: 'And the heavens are rolled up in His right hand' (Az-Zumar 39:67), and that He has a face by His saying: 'Everything is perishing except His face' (Al-Qasas 28:88), and His saying: 'And there remains the face of your Lord, Possessor of majesty and honor' (Ar-Rahman 55:27), and that He has a foot by His saying: 'Until the Lord places His foot in it' meaning Hellfire, and that He laughs at His believing servant by His saying concerning the one who is killed in the path of Allah: 'He met Allah and Allah was laughing at him,' and that He descends every night to the heaven of the world by the report of the Messenger of Allah, and that He is not one-eyed by the saying of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when he mentioned the Dajjal and said: 'Indeed, he...'
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of creedal statements from early Muslim authorities, presented by the author to establish the orthodox position regarding the Quran and Allah's attributes. The author begins with a statement attributed to Ibn Umar, listing four things created by Allah's hands, emphasizing that ordinary creation occurs through the command 'Be'. This affirms the literal hand of Allah. Next, the author cites Aisha's humility regarding the revelation of her innocence, underscoring that the Quran is divine speech. The central claim follows: the Quran is Allah's speech in all respects, revealed, uncreated, and every letter is uncreated, originating from Him and returning to Him. Ibn al-Mubarak's severe warning equates disbelief in a single letter with disbelief. The passage then broadens to include all revealed books as uncreated speech, with Ahmad ibn Hanbal affirming that the Quran in the Preserved Tablet, in mus-hafs, and in recitation is uncreated. Al-Bukhari adds that the Quran in written form and in hearts is the same, and deviation necessitates repentance. Finally, al-Shafi'i's detailed creed is quoted, listing specific attributes affirmed from Quran and hadith: hearing, sight, hands, right hand, face, foot, laughter, descending, and the negation of being one-eyed. All these are taken literally as reported, without interpretation. The passage serves as a foundational witness against those who deny or allegorize these attributes, particularly the Jahmiyyah and logicians.

Key Terms
كلام الله (kalam Allah): The speech of Allah, which is uncreated, revealed, and consists of letters and sounds; it includes the Quran and all revealed books. [Note: Stable in the Salafi creed; Ash'aris differentiate between the eternal attribute of speech and its created expression.]
غير مخلوق (ghayr makhluq): Not created; applied here to the Quran and all divine attributes, meaning they are eternal and not originated in time. [Note: Central point of contention between Salaf and Jahmiyyah/Mu'tazila who held the Quran was created.]
يد (yad): Hand; an attribute of Allah affirmed literally from the Quran, without modality (takyeef) or metaphor. [Note: Ash'aris interpret as a metaphor for power or favor while Salaf affirm as a real attribute.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak say about someone who disbelieves in a single letter of the Quran?
A) They should be given the benefit of the doubt.
B) They have disbelieved.
C) They are still Muslims.
D) They need to be taught proper recitation.

Key Takeaway
The Salafi creed holds the Quran as uncreated in every aspect and affirms Allah's attributes as literally stated, without modality or metaphor.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. List the four attributes of Allah that are affirmed with explicit Quranic verses in the passage (e.g., hands, right hand, face, foot).
?
2. Explain why Ibn al-Mubarak considered disbelief in a single letter of the Quran as kufr, based on his statement in the passage.

The Salaf's Acceptance of Hadiths on Divine Attributes
Author lists hadiths accepted by the ummah affirming divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how Ibn Taymiyya uses hadith evidence to argue that the early Muslim community (Salaf) affirmed divine attributes without metaphorical interpretation.

Core Idea
The ummah's acceptance of anthropomorphic hadiths is Ibn Taymiyya's proof that they should be taken literally, not reinterpreted.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya shifts from logical critique to textual evidence. He lists dozens of hadiths from the authentic collections that describe Allah with hands, fingers, jealousy, and form. His point is that the entire early community (the ummah) received these hadiths with acceptance and affirmation (تلقتها الأمة بالقبول والتصديق). This is a key rhetorical move: if the logicians claim that reason must interpret such texts, Ibn Taymiyya counters that the Salaf—the most knowledgeable generation—accepted them as they are. Your task is to understand how this list functions as an argument from authority and consensus (ijma').

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's claim
Find the phrase where Ibn Taymiyya states how the ummah received these hadiths. It is 'تلقتها الأمة بالقبول والتصديق' (the ummah received them with acceptance and affirmation). This is the core claim.
2
Note the source of the hadiths
The author specifies that these hadiths are from 'الصحاح والمسانيد' (the Sahihs and Musnads), i.e., the most authentic collections like Bukhari, Muslim, and Ahmad. This gives them epistemic weight.
3
Survey the attributes mentioned
Scan through the list and notice the variety: hand (يد), finger (إصبع), jealousy (غيرة), form (صورة), etc. Each is a divine attribute that might seem anthropomorphic to a rationalist.
List at least three attributes to yourself.
4
Understand the Salafi methodology
Ibn Taymiyya presents this as evidence that the Salaf did not engage in ta'wil (metaphorical interpretation). Instead, they affirmed the attributes 'bila kayf' (without asking how). The acceptance by the ummah implies consensus (ijma').
This is a rebuttal to those who say such hadiths must be reinterpreted.
5
Connect to the broader critique
This passage is part of Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the logicians who reject hadiths based on rational criteria. By showing that the ummah accepted them, he argues that the logicians' approach contradicts the practice of the early Muslims.

أعور ، وإن ربكم ليس بأعور » (۱) ، وأن المؤمنين يرون ربهم يوم القيامة بأبصارهم كما يرون القمر ليلة البدر، وأن له إصبعًا لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مـا مـن قلـب إلا وهو بين إصبعين من أصابع الرحمن (۲). قال: وسوى ما نقله الشافعي أحاديثُ جاءت في الصحاح والمسانيد، وتلقتها الأمة بالقبول والتصديق، نحو ما في «الصحيح» من حديث الذَّات (۳)، وقوله: «لا شخص أغيرُ من الله » (٤)، وقوله: «أتعجبون مِن غَيرة سعد ؟ والله لأنا أغْيرُ من سعد، والله أغْيرُ مني (٥)، وقوله: «ليس أحدٌ أحبُّ إليه المدح من الله ، ولذلك مَدَح نفسه، وليس أحد أغيرُ من الله، من أجل ذلك حرَّم الفواحش ما ظهر منها وما بطن» (٦) ، وقوله : «يد الله مَلْأَى» (۷)، وقوله: بيده الأخرى الميزان يخفِضُ ويرفع » (۸) ، وقوله: «إن الله يقبضُ يوم القيامة الأرَضِين، وتكونُ السمواتُ بيمينه، ثم يقول: أنا الملك» (۹) . ونحو قوله: «ثلاث حَثَياتٍ من حَيَّات الرَّب » (١) ، وقوله: «لما خلق آدمَ مسح ظهره بیمینه (۲)، وقوله في حديث أبي رزين قلت يا رسول الله، فما يفعل ربنا بنا إذا لقيناه؟ قال: تُعْرَضون عليه باديةً له صفحاتكم لا يخفى عليه منكم خافية، فيأخذ ربك بيده غرفة من الماء، فينضَحُ قِبَلكم، فلعَمْرُ إلهك ما يخطئ وجه أحدكم منها «قطرة أخرجه أحمد في «المسند»(۳)، وحديث القبضة التي يخرج بها من النار قوما لم يعملوا خيرًا قط، قد عادوا حُمَما، فيلقيهم في نهرٍ من أنهار الجنَّة يقال له : الحياة (٤). ونحو الحديث: رأيتُ ربي في أحسن صورة» (٥)، ونحو قوله: «خلق
One-eyed, and your Lord is not one-eyed (1), and that the believers will see their Lord on the Day of Resurrection with their eyes as they see the full moon on the night of the full moon, and that He has a finger, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'There is no heart but it is between two fingers of the fingers of the Merciful' (2). He said: Besides what al-Shafi'i reported, there are hadiths that came in the Sahihs and Musnads, and the ummah received them with acceptance and affirmation, such as what is in the Sahih concerning the hadith of the self (3), and His saying: 'No person is more jealous than Allah' (4), and His saying: 'Do you wonder at Sa'd's jealousy? By Allah, I am more jealous than Sa'd, and Allah is more jealous than I' (5), and His saying: 'There is no one who loves praise more than Allah, therefore He praised Himself, and there is no one more jealous than Allah, because of which He forbade immoralities, both open and secret' (6), and His saying: 'The hand of Allah is full' (7), and His saying: 'In His other hand is the balance, He lowers and raises' (8), and His saying: 'Allah will seize the earths on the Day of Resurrection, and the heavens will be in His right hand, then He will say: I am the King' (9). And like His saying: 'Three handfuls from the snakes of the Lord' (1), and His saying: 'When He created Adam, He wiped his back with His right hand' (2), and His saying in the hadith of Abu Razin: I said, O Messenger of Allah, what will our Lord do with us when we meet Him? He said: You will be presented before Him, your pages exposed, nothing hidden from Him, then your Lord will take with His hand a handful of water and sprinkle it upon you, and by the life of your Lord, not a single drop will miss the face of any of you' — Ahmad reported it in the Musnad (3), and the hadith of the handful by which He will bring out from the Fire people who never did any good, who have become cinders, and He will throw them into a river of the rivers of Paradise called 'The River of Life' (4). And like the hadith: 'I saw my Lord in the most beautiful form' (5), and like His saying: 'He created'...
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of hadiths that affirm various divine attributes, presented as evidence that the early Muslim community (ummah) accepted these texts without alteration. The author begins by mentioning a hadith that negates physical defect (one-eyed) and affirms seeing Allah on the Day of Resurrection. He then quotes the famous hadith about the heart being between the two fingers of the Merciful. The author states that besides the reports transmitted by al-Shafi'i, there are many other hadiths in the authentic collections (Sahihs and Musnads) that the ummah received with acceptance. He proceeds to list several examples: the hadith about Allah's jealousy, His love of praise, His full hand, the balance in His hand, His seizing the earths, three handfuls, wiping Adam's back, the sprinkling of water, the handful that brings people out of the Fire, and the vision of the Lord in the most beautiful form. Each of these hadiths contains expressions that appear anthropomorphic (hand, finger, form, jealousy, etc.). The author's purpose is to show that the Salaf (early Muslims) affirmed these attributes without resorting to metaphorical interpretation (ta'wil) or denial, which is part of his broader critique of the logicians who might reject such reports based on rationalistic criteria. The passage is not a syllogistic argument but a collection of textual evidence.

Key Terms

الأمة
يد الله

غيرة
القبول والتصديق

D) They ignored them.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya uses the ummah's acceptance of these hadiths to argue that the Salaf affirmed divine attributes literally, undermining the rationalist call for metaphorical interpretation.

Critique of Dismissing Opposing Views as Defiance of Reason
Ibn Taymiyya refutes dismissing opposing views as defiance of reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical fallacy of dismissing opposing views as 'defiance of reason' and evaluate Ibn Taymiyya's critique of this rhetorical strategy.

Core Idea
Calling an opponent's view 'defiance of reason' is not a proof—it is an appeal to emotion, not evidence.

In theological debates, it is tempting to label opposing views as contrary to reason itself. Ibn Taymiyya here exposes this tactic as invalid: it substitutes rational engagement with emotional aversion. He shows that even groups deemed extreme, like the anthropomorphists, are not dismissed as irrational by serious scholars; rather, they are refuted with arguments. This lesson unpacks his critique and applies it to distinguish genuine rational refutation from rhetorical dismissal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rhetorical move under attack
Ibn Taymiyya targets those who claim that an opponent's view is 'mukābara lil-'uqūl' (defiance of reason). What does this label imply about the opponent's epistemic status?
It implies the opponent's view is self-evidently false, so no refutation is needed.
2
Examine the example of the anthropomorphists
Why does Ibn Taymiyya say no serious scholar called their view defiance of reason? He notes that refuters engaged with them using rational proofs, not dismissive labels. This shows proper debate requires argument.
Both sides have truth and falsehood; the label is an unfair caricature.
3
Analyze the case of the deniers of the Creator
Even the most misguided deniers of the Creator are not accused of defying reason by their refuters; rather, their falsehood is claimed to be known through reasoning. This reinforces that the 'defiance' charge is not used by serious scholars.
The label is a rhetorical tool, not a serious epistemic claim.
4
Identify the true basis for Ibn Taymiyya's objection
He argues that mere aversion (nufūr) or attraction does not indicate truth. The only valid basis for judgment is divine guidance (hudā min Allāh). Without it, following emotional reactions is following desire.
The Quranic verses cited warn against following desires without guidance.
5
Connect to Quranic verses
Ibn Taymiyya cites verses prohibiting following desires without divine guidance. How do these support his epistemological point? They establish that emotional reactions are unreliable guides to truth; only revelation and reasoned argument carry weight.
This grounds his critique in Islamic authority.

تكون في إثبات ما أثبتوه، وإما أن تكون في تناقضهم بالجمع بين إثبات هذه الأمور ونفي الجوارح.
أما الأول فباطل؛ فإن المجسّمة المحضة التي تصرّح بالتجسيم المحض وتغلو فيه لم يقل أحدٌ قطُّ : إن قولها مكابرة للعقول، ولا قال أحد: إنهم لا يخاطبون، بل الذين ردُّوا على غالية المجسمة مثل هشام بن الحكم وشيعته لم يردُّوا عليهم من الحجج العقلية إلا بحُجَج تحتاج إلى نظر واستدلال والمنازع لهم وإن كان مبطلا في كثير مما يقوله فقد قابلهم بنظير حجاجهم، و لم يكونوا عليه بأظهر منه عليهم، إذ مع كل طائفة حق وباطل.
وإذا كان مثل أبي الفرج إنما يعتمد في نفي هذه الأمور على ما يذكره نفاة النظّار، فأولئك لا يكادون يزعمون في شيء من النفي والإثبات أنـه مكابرة للعقول، حتى جاحدو الصَّانع - الذين هم أجهل الخلق وأضلهم وأكفرهم وأعظمهم خلافًا للعقول - لا يزعم أكثر هؤلاء الذين أنتصر بهم أبو الفرج أن قولهم مكابرة للعقول، بل يزعمون أن العلم بفساد قولهم إنما يُعْلَمُ بالنظر والاستدلال.
وهذا القول وإن كان يقوله جل هؤلاء النفاة من أهل الكلام، فليس هو طريقة مرضية، لكن المقصود أن هؤلاء النُّفاة لا يزعمون أن العلم بفساد قول المثبتة معلوم بالضرورة ولا أن قولهم مكابرة للعقل، وإن شنعوا عليهم بأشياء ينفِرُ عنها كثير من الناس فذاك ليستعينوا بنفرة النافرين على دفعهم وإخماد قولهم، لا لأن نفور النافرين عندهم يدلُّ على حق أو باطل، ولا لأن قولهم مكابرة للعقل أو معلوم بضرورة العقل أو ببديهته فساده، هذا لم أعلم أحدا من أئمة النفاة أهل النظر يدعيه في شيء من أقوال المثبتة وإن كان فيها من الغلو ما فيها.
ومن المعلوم أن مجرد نفور النافرين أو محبَّة الموافقين لا يدلُّ على صحة قول ولا فساده إلا إذا كان ذلك بهدى من الله، بل الاستدلال بذلك هو استدلال باتباع الهوى بغير هدى من الله؛ فإن أتباع الإنسان لما يهواه هو القول والفعل الذي يحبُّه وردُّ القول والفعل الذي يبغضه بلا هدى من قال تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّ كَثِيرًا لَيَضِلُّونَ بِأَهْوَابِهِم بِغَيْرِ عِلْمٍ﴾ [الأنعام: ١١٩]، وقال: فَإِن لَّمْ يَسْتَجِيبُوا لَكَ فَأَعْلَمْ أَنَّمَا يَتَّبِعُونَ أَهْوَاءَهُمْ وَمَنْ أَضَلُّ مِمَّنِ اتَّبَعَ هَوَنهُ بِغَيْرِ هُدًى مِّنَ اللهِ ﴾ [القصص: ٥٠] وقال تعالى :لداود: ﴿وَلَا تَتَّبِعِ الْهَوَى فَيُضِلَّكَ عَن سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ ﴾ [ص: ٢٦] وقال تعالى: ﴿فَإِن شَهدُوا فَلَا تَشْهَدْ مَعَهُمْ وَلَا تَتَّبِعْ أَهْوَاءَ الَّذِينَ كَذَبُوا بِشَايَتِنَا وَالَّذِينَ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ بِالْآخِرَةِ وَهُم بِرَبِّهِمْ يَعْدِلُونَ ﴾ [الأنعام: ١٥٠]، وقال تعالى: ﴿قُلْ يَأَهْلَ الْكِتَبِ لَا تَغْلُوا فِي دِينِكُمْ غَيْرَ الْحَقِّ وَلَا تَتَّبِعُوا أَهْوَاءَ قَوْمٍ قَدْ ضَلُّوا مِن قَبْلُ وَأَضَلُّوا كَثِيرًا وَضَلُّوا عَن سَوَاءِ السَّبِيلِ ﴾ [المائدة: ٧٧].
It is either in establishing what they have established, or in their contradiction by combining the affirmation of these matters with the negation of the bodily faculties. As for the first, it is false; for the extreme anthropomorphists who explicitly affirm crude anthropomorphism and exaggerate in it, no one has ever said: 'Their statement is a defiance of intellects,' nor has anyone said: 'They are not to be addressed.' Rather, those who refuted the extreme anthropomorphists such as Hisham ibn al-Hakam and his followers only refuted them with rational proofs that require consideration and inference, and their opponent, even if he is wrong in much of what he says, nonetheless met them with an equivalent of their argumentation, and they were not more evident against him than he was against them, for each faction has truth and falsehood. And since someone like Abu al-Faraj relies in negating these matters on what the negators among the speculative theologians mention, those people hardly claim in any matter of negation or affirmation that it is a defiance of intellects. Even the deniers of the Creator—who are the most ignorant of creation, the most misguided, the most disbelieving, and the greatest in opposition to intellects—most of those whom Abu al-Faraj supports do not claim that their statement is a defiance of intellects. Rather, they claim that knowledge of the corruption of their statement is only known through consideration and inference. And this statement, although it is said by most of these negators among the people of kalam, is not a satisfactory method. But the point is that these negators do not claim that knowledge of the corruption of the affirmers' statement is known necessarily, nor that their statement is a defiance of intellect; rather, they revile them with things from which many people shrink, so that they may seek help from the aversion of the averse to repel them and extinguish their statement. Not because the aversion of the averse in their view indicates truth or falsehood, nor because their statement is a defiance of intellect or that its corruption is known by intellectual necessity or intuition. This I have not known any of the leading negators among the people of consideration to claim in any of the affirmers' statements, even if there is exaggeration in them. And it is known that mere aversion of the averse or love of the like-minded does not indicate the correctness or corruption of a statement, unless it is by guidance from Allah. Rather, making such an indication is an argument by following desire without guidance from Allah. For a person’s following his desire is the statement and action that he loves, and rejecting the statement and action that he detests without guidance from Allah. He – exalted is He – said: {And indeed many lead astray [others] by their desires without knowledge} [al-An'am 6:119], and said: {But if they do not respond to you, then know that they only follow their desires. And who is more astray than one who follows his desire without guidance from Allah?} [al-Qasas 28:50], and said to Dawud: {And do not follow desire, lest it lead you astray from the way of Allah} [Sad 38:26], and said: {So if they testify, do not testify with them, and do not follow the desires of those who have denied Our signs and those who do not believe in the Hereafter, while they equate [others] with their Lord} [al-An'am 6:150], and said: {Say, O People of the Scripture, do not exceed limits in your religion beyond the truth, and do not follow the desires of a people who went astray before and misled many and strayed from the sound way} [al-Ma'idah 5:77].
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a critical argument by Ibn Taymiyya against the tendency to dismiss opposing theological views as 'defiance of reason' (mukābara lil-'uqūl). He begins by examining the claim that anthropomorphists (mujassima) are beyond rational discourse. He observes that no one has ever said their statements are a defiance of reason; rather, even their refuters engaged with them using rational arguments that require consideration and inference. This shows that both sides have elements of truth and falsehood, and neither is simply dismissed as irrational. He then moves to the deniers of the Creator (jāḥidū al-Ṣāniʿ), who are the most misguided. Even they are not typically accused of defying reason; their refuters claim their falsehood is known through reasoning, not self-evidently. Ibn Taymiyya clarifies that the goal of those who revile opponents is not to assert self-evident falsehood, but to gain the aversion of people to suppress the opponent's view. The core of his critique is that mere psychological aversion or attraction is not a valid indicator of truth or falsehood. Only guidance from Allah can be the basis for such judgment. He supports this with several Quranic verses that prohibit following desires without divine guidance. Thus, the passage refutes the idea that because many people find a view repugnant, it must be false—this is an argument from desire, not from evidence.

Key Terms
مكابرة للعقول
نفور النافرين
هدى من الله
المجسّمة

A) Because anthropomorphists are correct in their theology.

C) Because the Quran prohibits calling any group outright irrational.
D) Because the anthropomorphists themselves accepted reason as authoritative.

Key Takeaway
The label 'defiance of reason' is a rhetorical weapon, not a rational proof; true judgment must be based on divine guidance and reasoned argument.

Emotional Reactions Are Not Evidence
Author refutes the claim that people's repulsion indicates falsehood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why emotional reactions (nufur) are not valid evidence for truth or falsehood in Islamic epistemology, and distinguish between following hawa and huda Allah.

Core Idea
Emotional reactions are not evidence; only divine guidance yields truth.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya dismantles a common but flawed argument: that people's aversion or attraction to a statement indicates its falsehood or truth. He shows that such reactions stem from personal desire (hawa), not from objective knowledge or divine guidance. This lesson will help you recognize why subjective feelings cannot serve as logical evidence, and how to identify the true criterion for truth in Islamic thought.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
Find in the Arabic the assertion that people's aversion (nufur) indicates truth or falsehood. Note that the author denies this categorically.
The author says: 'not because the aversion of the averse among them indicates truth or falsehood'.
2
Extract the author's key distinction
Ibn Taymiyya distinguishes between mere emotional reaction and judgment based on divine guidance (huda Allah). He argues that without guidance, such reactions are merely following desire (hawa).
He states: 'mere aversion of the averse or love of the supporters does not indicate correctness... unless it is with guidance from God'.
3
Analyze the Quranic evidence
The author cites six Quranic verses condemning following desires without knowledge or guidance. Identify the common theme: all warn against hawa without huda.
Verses: 6:119, 28:50, 38:26, 6:150, 5:77, 2:120.
4
Apply the principle to a real debate
Consider the historical debate between affirmers (muthbita) and negators (nufat) of divine attributes. The author notes that even exaggerations by affirmers are not refuted by emotional reactions. Test this principle: can you refute a theological position solely because it feels wrong?
The author says he knows no leading negator who claimed that aversion alone indicates falsehood of affirmers' statements.

وإخماد قولهم، لا لأن نفور النافرين عندهم يدلُّ على حق أو باطل، ولا لأن قولهم مكابرة للعقل أو معلوم بضرورة العقل أو ببديهته فساده، هذا لم أعلم أحدا من أئمة النفاة أهل النظر يدعيه في شيء من أقوال المثبتة وإن كان فيها من الغلو ما فيها.

ومن المعلوم أن مجرد نفور النافرين أو محبَّة الموافقين لا يدلُّ على صحة قول ولا فساده إلا إذا كان ذلك بهدى من الله، بل الاستدلال بذلك هو استدلال باتباع الهوى بغير هدى من الله ؛ فإن أتباع الإنسان لما يهواه هو القول والفعل الذي يحبُّه وردُّ القول والفعل الذي يبغضه بلا هدى من الله. قال تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّ كَثِيرًا لَيَضِلُّونَ بِأَهْوَائِهِم بِغَيْرِ عِلْمٍ﴾ [الأنعام: ١١٩]، وقال: ﴿فَإِن لَّمْ يَسْتَجِيبُوا لَكَ فَاعْلَمْ أَنَّمَا يَتَّبِعُونَ أَهْوَاءَهُمْ وَمَنْ أَضَلُّ مِمَّنِ اتَّبَعَ هَوَاهُ بِغَيْرِ هُدًى مِّنَ اللهِ﴾ [القصص: ٥٠] وقال تعالى: ﴿يَا دَاوُودُ إِنَّا جَعَلْنَاكَ خَلِيفَةً فِي الْأَرْضِ فَاحْكُم بَيْنَ النَّاسِ بِالْحَقِّ وَلَا تَتَّبِعِ الْهَوَى فَيُضِلَّكَ عَن سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ﴾ [ص: ٢٦] وقال تعالى: ﴿فَإِن شَهِدُوا فَلَا تَشْهَدْ مَعَهُمْ وَلَا تَتَّبِعْ أَهْوَاءَ الَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا بِآيَاتِنَا وَالَّذِينَ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ بِالْآخِرَةِ وَهُم بِرَبِّهِمْ يَعْدِلُونَ﴾ [الأنعام: ١٥٠]، وقال تعالى: ﴿قُلْ يَا أَهْلَ الْكِتَابِ لَا تَغْلُوا فِي دِينِكُمْ غَيْرَ الْحَقِّ وَلَا تَتَّبِعُوا أَهْوَاءَ قَوْمٍ قَدْ ضَلُّوا مِن قَبْلُ وَأَضَلُّوا كَثِيرًا وَضَلُّوا عَن سَوَاءِ السَّبِيلِ﴾ [المائدة: ٧٧]، وقال تعالى: ﴿وَلَن تَرْضَىٰ عَنكَ الْيَهُودُ وَلَا النَّصَارَىٰ حَتَّىٰ تَتَّبِعَ مِلَّتَهُمْ قُلْ إِنَّ هُدَى اللَّهِ هُوَ الْهُدَىٰ وَلَئِنِ اتَّبَعْتَ أَهْوَاءَهُم بَعْدَ الَّذِي جَاءَكَ مِنَ الْعِلْمِ مَا لَكَ مِنَ اللَّهِ مِن وَلِيٍّ وَلَا نَصِيرٍ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۲۰]، فمن أتبع أهواء الناس بعد العلم الذي بعث الله به رسوله، وبعد هدى الله الذي بيَّنه لعباده، فهو بهذه المثابة.
And suppressing their statement, not because the aversion of the averse among them indicates truth or falsehood, nor because their statement is a stubbornness against reason or its corruption is known by necessity of reason or its self-evidence. I do not know any of the leading negators among the people of speculative theology who claims this regarding any of the statements of the affirmers, even if there is exaggeration in them. It is known that mere aversion of the averse or love of the supporters does not indicate the correctness or corruption of a statement, unless it is with guidance from God. Rather, using that as evidence is evidence by following desire without guidance from God. For a person's following of what he desires is the statement and action he loves, and rejecting the statement and action he hates without guidance from God. He said, Exalted: 'And indeed many lead astray with their desires without knowledge.' [6:119] And He said: 'So if they do not respond to you, then know that they only follow their desires, and who is more astray than one who follows his desire without guidance from God?' [28:50] And He said: 'O David, indeed We have made you a successor upon the earth; so judge between people with truth and do not follow desire, lest it lead you astray from the way of God.' [38:26] And He said: 'So if they bear witness, do not bear witness with them, and do not follow the desires of those who deny Our signs and those who do not believe in the Hereafter, and they equate others with their Lord.' [6:150] And He said: 'Say, O People of the Book, do not exceed bounds in your religion beyond the truth, and do not follow the desires of a people who went astray before and misled many and strayed from the sound path.' [5:77] And He said: 'And never will the Jews nor the Christians be pleased with you until you follow their religion. Say, indeed the guidance of God is the guidance. And if you follow their desires after what has come to you of knowledge, you will have against God no protector nor helper.' [2:120] So whoever follows the desires of people after the knowledge that God sent His Messenger with, and after the guidance of God which He clarified to His servants, he is in this status.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a critical epistemological refutation from Ibn Taymiyya's Naqd al-Mantiq. He argues that emotional reactions—aversion or attraction—cannot serve as evidence for the truth or falsehood of a statement, because they stem from following personal desire (hawa) rather than divine guidance (huda). He supports this with multiple Quranic verses that condemn following desires without knowledge or guidance. The author distinguishes between worthy and unworthy use of emotional responses: only when accompanied by guidance from God do they have validity. This is part of Ibn Taymiyya's broader critique of using subjective reactions as logical evidence.

هوى
هدى الله
مثبتة

A) The strength of people's aversion or love for it.
B) The consensus of the majority of scholars.
C) Guidance from God (huda Allah) and knowledge.
D) Its conformity to rational self-evidence.

Key Takeaway
Emotional reactions are not valid evidence; only knowledge and divine guidance determine truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Logic as a Communal Obligation
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the claim that logic is a communal obligation and critiques its practitioners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument against the claim that logic is a fard kifaya and evaluate his grounds for rejecting its obligation in Islamic law.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya argues that logic is neither obligatory in Islam nor beneficial; its practitioners are corrupt and even its experts abandon its rules.

This passage from Ibn Taymiyya's Naqd al-Mantiq challenges a common claim among philosophers and some theologians that studying Aristotelian logic is a communal obligation (fard kifaya) and indispensable for sound knowledge. Ibn Taymiyya dismantles this claim by pointing to the actual state of logicians, the lack of scriptural basis, and the historical consensus of Muslim scholars against it. Let's walk through his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target claim
Find the exact statement Ibn Taymiyya is refuting: that logic is fard kifaya and that without it one cannot trust any knowledge.
The claim is attributed to unnamed proponents; Ibn Taymiyya calls it 'extremely corrupt'.
2
Locate the empirical counter-evidence
Ibn Taymiyya points to the real-world observation that those who force themselves to use logic end up corrupt in reasoning. This is an inductive argument from experience.
He says such a person is 'corrupt in examination and debate'.
3
Understand the attribution to the proponents
He gives a charitable interpretation: those who claim obligation were once extremely ignorant and found some help in logic, but they still fell into other falsehoods.
They 'returned from some of their falsehood' but did not obtain beneficial truth.
4
Examine the Sharia-based objection
He denies that obligation can be ascribed to Islamic law; logic is not commanded by God, and its necessity arises only from personal failure.
He says 'it is not correct to ascribe its obligation to the Sharia in any way'.
5
Analyze the critique of logicians themselves
Even the proficient (hudhdhaq) do not adhere to logical rules; they abandon them for various reasons, indicating the system's flaws.
The simile: 'like the meat of a barren camel on a treacherous mountain'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
وأما المنطق، فمن قال : إنه فرض كفاية، وأنه من ليس له به خبرة فليس له ثقة بشيء من علومه فهذا القولُ في غاية الفساد من وجوه كثيرة التّعداد، مشتمل على أمور فاسدة ودعاوى باطلة كثيرة لا يتّسع هذا الموضع لاستقصائها.
بل الواقع قديمًا وحديثًا أنك لا تجد من يُلْزِمُ نفسه أن ينظر في علومه به ويناظر به إلا وهو فاسد النظر والمناظرة، كثير العجز عن تحقيق علم وبيانه. فأحسنُ ما يُحْمَلُ عليه كلام المتكلّم في هذا أن يكون قد كان هو وأمثاله في غاية الجهالة والضلالة، وقد فقدوا أسباب الهدى كلها، فلم يجدوا ما يردُّهم عن تلك الجهالات إلا بعض ما في المنطق من الأمور التي صحيحة، فإنه بسبب بعض ذلك رجع كثير من هؤلاء عن بعض باطلهم، وإن لم يحصل لهم حقٌّ ينفعهم، وإن وقعوا في باطل آخر.
ومع هذا، فلا يصح نسبة وجوبه إلى شريعة الإسلام بوجه من الوجوه؛ إذ من هذه حاله أُتِيَ من نفسه بترك ما أمر الله به من الحق حتى أحتاج إلى الباطل. ومن المعلوم أن القول بوجوبه قول غُلاته وجهال أصحابه، ونفس الحذاق منهم لا يلتزمون قوانينه في كلّ علومهم، بل يُعْرِضُون عنها، إما لطولها، وإما لعدم فائدتها، وإما لفسادها، وإما لعدم تميزها وما فيها من الإجمال والاشتباه، فإنه فيه مواضع كثيرة هي لحم جمل غر على رأس جبل وغر، لا سهل فيُرتقى ولا سمين فيُنتقل.
ولهذا مازال علماء المسلمين وأئمة الدين يذمونه ويذمون أهله، وينهون عنه وعن أهله، حتى رأيتُ للمتأخرين فتيا فيها خطوط جماعة من أعيان زمانهم من أئمة الشافعية والحنفية وغيرهم فيها كلام عظيم في تحريمه وعقوبة أهله.
حتى إن من الحكايات المشهورة التي بلغتنا أن الشيخ أبا عمرو بن الصلاح
Section. As for logic, whoever says that it is a communal obligation, and that whoever has no expertise in it cannot trust anything of his sciences, this statement is extremely corrupt in many respects, encompassing corrupt matters and many false claims that this place cannot exhaust. Rather, the reality, past and present, is that you do not find anyone who compels himself to examine his sciences by means of it and to debate by means of it except that he is corrupt in examination and debate, very incapable of verifying knowledge and clarifying it. The best interpretation of the speaker's words in this is that he and his likes were in extreme ignorance and misguidance, and they lost all means of guidance, so they found nothing to repel them from those ignorances except some of the correct matters in logic, for due to some of that many of these people returned from some of their falsehood, even if they did not obtain a truth that benefits them, and they fell into another falsehood. Besides this, it is not correct to ascribe its obligation to the Islamic law (Sharia) in any way; for such a person comes from himself by abandoning what God commanded of truth until he needed falsehood. And it is known that the statement of its obligation is the statement of its extremists and the ignorant of its followers, and even the proficient among them do not adhere to its rules in all their sciences, but rather they turn away from them, either because of their length, or because of their lack of benefit, or because of their corruption, or because of their lack of distinctness and what is in them of ambiguity and confusion, for it contains many places that are like the meat of a barren camel on top of a treacherous mountain, neither easy to climb nor fat enough to carry away. Therefore, the Muslim scholars and the imams of the religion have always censured it and its people, and forbade it and its people, until I saw a legal opinion (fatwa) by later scholars containing the signatures of a group of the notables of their time from the imams of the Shafi'is and Hanafis and others, which includes strong words forbidding it and punishing its people. So much so that among the famous stories that reached us is that Shaykh Abu Amr ibn al-Salah...
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
We begin with a passage from Ibn Taymiyya's Naqd Mantiq in which he launches a devastating critique of the claim that logic (mantiq) is a communal obligation (fard kifaya) in Islam. He opens by stating that this claim is extremely corrupt (ghayat al-fasad) from many angles. The reality, he says, both past and present, is that anyone who commits himself to using logic in his studies and debates ends up being corrupt in his reasoning and incapable of achieving true verification of knowledge. The best interpretation of the proponent's statement is that such a person and his likes were in extreme ignorance and loss of guidance, so they turned to the correct aspects of logic to find some remedy, but they did not attain true benefit and fell into other falsehoods. Then Ibn Taymiyya argues that ascribing obligation to logic from Islamic law (Sharia) is baseless. The claim of obligation, he says, comes only from the extremists and the ignorant among its followers. Even the proficient experts (al-hudhdhaq) do not adhere to its rules in all their sciences; they abandon them due to length, lack of benefit, corruption, or ambiguity. He vividly describes these rules as 'like the meat of a barren camel on top of a treacherous mountain: not easy to climb nor fat enough to carry away' – a classic Arabic simile for something useless and inaccessible. Finally, he points to the historical consensus of Muslim scholars and imams who have denounced logic and its people, citing a fatwa by later scholars (including Shafi'is and Hanafis) that forbids logic and prescribes punishment for its practitioners. The passage ends with an incomplete mention of Shaykh Abu Amr ibn al-Salah, presumably another authority who condemned logic.

Key Terms
فرض كفاية
منطق
حذاق
شريعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya in this passage, what is the best interpretation of the claim that logic is obligatory?
A) It comes from those who are extremely ignorant and lost, seeking some remedy.
B) It is a divinely revealed command.
C) It is based on the consensus of the Sahaba.
D) It is a necessary condition for ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's refutation of logic's obligatory nature relies on empirical observation of logicians' failures, the lack of Sharia basis, the inconstancy of even expert logicians, and the historical condemnation by Muslim scholars.

?

The Dangers of Claiming Exclusive Knowledge via Syllogistic Reasoning
Author argues that exclusivist claim of logical method leads to kufr and nifaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's critique of logical exclusivism and evaluate its implications for faith.

Core Idea
Claiming only syllogistic reasoning yields knowledge leads to disbelief and hypocrisy.

Ibn Taymiyya, in his Naqd al-Mantiq, targets a dangerous claim made by some logicians: that no true knowledge exists except through the syllogistic method. In this passage, he warns that such an exclusivist stance can undermine faith itself. By examining his argument, you will understand why he considers this view not just an intellectual error but a theological crisis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being attacked
The logicians' claim that only syllogistic reasoning (al-tariq al-qiyasi) produces knowledge. Find this in the Arabic: 'أن كلَّ ما لم يحصل بهذه الطريق القياسية فليس بعلم'.
2
Understand the consequences Ibn Taymiyya draws
If someone cannot obtain faith through this path (and many cannot), they become a disbeliever, hypocrite, etc. Note the chain of negative attributes: 'كافرًا زنديقا منافقا جاهلا ضالا مضلا ظلوما كفورا'.
3
Notice the Quranic support
He cites verses from Surat al-Furqan (25:31-33) to align these logicians with the enemies of the prophets. This grounds his critique in revelation.
4
Recognize the mixed outcome
Even if some obtain faith via this path or another, they may also acquire hypocrisy (nifaq) from it. So faith and hypocrisy can coexist.
5
Evaluate the broader implication
Ibn Taymiyya is not rejecting logic itself but the claim that it is the exclusive path to knowledge. The error is epistemological exclusivism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا تقلدوا عن طواغيتهم أن كلَّ ما لم يحصل بهذه الطريق القياسية فليس بعلم، وقد لا يحصل لكثير منهم من هذه الطريق القياسية ما يستفيد به الإيمان الواجب، فيكون كافرًا زنديقا منافقًا جاهلا ضالًا مُضِلًا ظلوما كفورًا، ويكون من أكابر أعداء الرُّسل من الذين قال الله فيهم : ﴿ وَكَذَلِكَ جَعَلْنَا لِكُلِّ نَي عَدُوًّا مِنَ الْمُجْرِمِينَ وَكَفَى بِرَبِّكَ هَادِيًا وَنَصِيرًا ) وَقَالَ اللَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا لَوْلَا نُزِلَ عَلَيْهِ الْقُرْآنُ جُمْلَةُ وَاحِدَةً كَذَلِكَ لِنُثَبِّتَ بِهِ فُؤَادَكَ وَرَتَّلْتَهُ ترتيلا ) وَلَا يَأْتُونَكَ بِمَثَلٍ إِلَّا جِئْنَكَ بِالْحَقِّ وَأَحْسَنَ تَفْسِيرًا ﴾ [الفرقان: ۳۱-۳۳]. وربما حصل لبعضهم إيمان إما من هذه الطريق أو من غيرها، ويحصل له أيضا منها نفاق، فيكون فيه إيمان ونفاق، ويكون في حال مؤمنًا وفي حال منافقا، ويكون مرتدّا إما عن أصل الدين أو بعض شرائعه، إما ردَّة نفاق وإمـا ردَّة كفر، وهذا كثير غالب، لا سيّما في الأعصار والأمصار التي تَغْلِبُ فيها الجاهلية والكفر والنفاق، فلهؤلاء من عجائب الجهل والظلم والكذب والكفر والنفاق والضلال ما لا يتسع لذكره المقال
So if they adopt from their tyrants [the claim] that everything not obtained by this syllogistic path is not knowledge, and for many of them this syllogistic path may not obtain what they would use for obligatory faith, then he becomes a disbeliever, a heretic, a hypocrite, an ignorant one, misguided and misguiding, unjust and ungrateful. And he becomes among the greatest enemies of the messengers, of whom God said: 'And thus We made for every prophet an enemy from among the criminals, and sufficient is your Lord as a guide and helper' and 'Those who disbelieve say: Why was the Quran not sent down upon him all at once? Thus We strengthen your heart thereby and We recited it in a well-arranged recital. And they do not come to you with an example except that We bring you the truth and the best explanation.' And perhaps some of them obtain faith either by this path or by another, and from it also obtains hypocrisy, so in him there is faith and hypocrisy, and he is at times a believer and at times a hypocrite, and he becomes an apostate either from the foundation of the religion or from some of its laws, either apostasy of hypocrisy or apostasy of disbelief. And this is frequent and prevalent, especially in ages and places where ignorance, disbelief, and hypocrisy dominate. So these people have such wonders of ignorance, injustice, lying, disbelief, hypocrisy, and misguidance that the discourse cannot contain their mention.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage from Ibn Taymiyya's Naqd Mantiq critiques the claim made by some logicians that true knowledge ('ilm) can only be obtained through syllogistic reasoning (al-tariq al-qiyasi). He argues that this exclusivist view leads to grave consequences. For those who cannot attain the necessary faith through this method—which he suggests is many—they become disbelievers, hypocrites, and enemies of the prophets. He supports this with Quranic verses from Surat al-Furqan, which describe how God defends His prophet against such opponents. Ibn Taymiyya then points out that even if some do obtain faith via this path or another, they may simultaneously acquire hypocrisy (nifaq) from it, leading to a mixed state of belief and disbelief. Such people may apostatize from the core of the religion or its specific laws, often out of hypocrisy rather than outright disbelief. He considers this phenomenon widespread, especially in times when ignorance and faithlessness dominate. The passage serves to expose the danger of elevating a human method of reasoning to the exclusive criterion for knowledge, which effectively denies the possibility of divine guidance and prophetic knowledge.

Key Terms
الطريق القياسية
طواغيت
نفاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya in this passage, what is one consequence of adopting the claim that no knowledge exists except through syllogistic reasoning?
A) It leads to a more rigorous scientific method.
B) It may cause those unable to use it to lose faith entirely and become disbelievers.
C) It is a valid method for prophets and saints.
D) It separates faith from hypocrisy.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya warns that elevating a human reasoning method to the sole criterion for knowledge leads to disbelief, because it denies the epistemic value of divine revelation.
