Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Sabian Logicians and the Necessity of Prophethood
Criticizes Sabian logicians for omitting prophethood and discusses the historical Sabians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the Sabian logicians' omission of prophethood and evaluate his distinction between ancient and later Sabians.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya attacks not logic itself, but its use without prophetic guidance.

This passage from Ibn Taymiyya's Naqd al-Mantiq targets the Sabian logicians who defined syllogism types without any reference to divine revelation. He argues that even technically correct definitions are dangerous if they ignore prophethood, because true knowledge requires prophetic guidance. He also criticizes a later redefinition of 'mashhurat' (commonly accepted premises), and distinguishes between ancient Sabians who were monotheists and later Sabians (philosophers) who rejected prophethood. This lesson will help you understand how Ibn Taymiyya connects logical methodology to belief in divine guidance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of criticism
Who are the 'Sabians' in this passage? What did they omit from their logical definitions? Notice that Ibn Taymiyya says they did not mention prophecies (nubuwwāt) and did not affirm or deny them.
The Sabians here are later philosophers, not the ancient monotheistic Sabians.
2
Analyze the critique of mashhurat
Later logicians defined mashhurat as 'accepted premises' because the speaker is supported by something compelling acceptance. Ibn Taymiyya says this addition was forced by argumentative pressure. Why does he object? Consider the shift from a purely logical category to one tied to authority.
This critique shows that definitions are not neutral; they can embed implicit assumptions.
3
Distinguish ancient vs. later Sabians
Ibn Taymiyya distinguishes between ancient Sabians who believed in God and the Last Day (like righteous Jews and Christians before Muhammad) and later Sabians (philosophers) who mixed Sabianism with Hanifiyya. Why does he make this distinction? It allows him to condemn the later ones without condemning all Sabians wholesale.
This is a common theological move: distinguishing between a group's early righteous members and later deviants.
4
Evaluate the theological claim
How does Ibn Taymiyya connect logical methodology to belief in prophethood? He argues that omitting prophethood from logical discourse is itself a form of misguidance (ḍalāl), even if one does not actively deny the messengers. Reflect on what this implies about the relationship between reason and revelation.
This is a core Islamic epistemological claim: reason cannot replace revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا كلام أولئك المبتدعة من الصَّابئة الذين لم يذكروا النبوات ولا تعرَّضوا لها بنفي ولا إثبات وعدم التصديق للرسل واتباعهم كفر وضلال وإن لم يُعتقد تكذيبهم ، فالكفر والضلال أعم من التكذيب. وأما قول بعض المتأخرين في المشهورات: هي المقبولات، لكون صاحبها مؤيدا بأمرٍ يوجب قبول قوله، ونحو ذلك = فهذه من الزيادات التي ألزمتهم إياها الحجة، ورأوا وجوب قبولها على طريقة الأولين. ولهذا [كان] غالب صابئة المتأخرين - الذين هم الفلاسفة ـ ممتزجين بالحنيفية، كما أن غالب من دخل في الفلسفة من الحنفاء مَزَج الحنيفية بالصُّبوء ولَبَسَ الحقِّ بالباطل. أعني بالصُّبوء: المبتدع الذي ليس فيه إيمان بالنبوات، كصُبوء صاحب المنطق وأتباعه. وأما الصُّبوء القديم فذاك أصحابه منهم المؤمنون بالله واليوم الآخر، الذين آمنوا وعملوا الصالحات فلا خوف عليهم ولا هم يحزنون، كما أن التهود والتنصر منه ما أهله مبتدِعُون ضُلَّالُ قبل إرسال محمد ، ومنه ما كان أهله متبعين للحقِّ وهم الذين آمنوا بالله واليوم الآخر وعملوا الصالحات، فلا خوف عليهم ولا هم يحزنون.
And this is the speech of those innovators among the Sabians who did not mention prophecies, nor did they address them by negation or affirmation; and lack of belief in the messengers and following them is disbelief and misguidance, even if one does not hold them to be liars. So disbelief and misguidance are more general than accusations of lying. As for the statement of some later [scholars] concerning common [premises]: 'They are accepted [premises], because their advocate is supported by something that necessitates acceptance of his statement,' and the like—these are among the additions that proof forced upon them, and they saw the necessity of accepting them according to the way of the predecessors. For this reason, most of the later Sabians—who are the philosophers—mixed with the Hanifiyya (monotheism), just as most of those who entered philosophy from the Hanifiyya mixed the Hanifiyya with Sabianism and confused truth with falsehood. I mean by Sabianism: innovation that does not include faith in prophecies, like the Sabianism of the author of logic and his followers. As for the ancient Sabianism, its adherents included those who believed in God and the Last Day, who believed and did righteous deeds—no fear shall be on them, nor shall they grieve—just as among Judaism and Christianity, some of their people are innovators and misguided before the sending of Muhammad, and some of their people were followers of truth, they who believed in God and the Last Day and did righteous deeds—no fear shall be on them, nor shall they grieve.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary wherein the author attacks the Sabian logicians who defined the three syllogism types without reference to divine revelation. The author argues that their definitions, while technically correct in a secular sense, are the product of innovators who ignore prophethood. He distinguishes between disbelief (kufr) and misguidance (dalal) and asserting that their teachings are still dangerous even if they do not formally accuse messengers of lying. He then criticizes later logicians who defined common premises (mashhurat) as 'accepted' because the speaker is supported by something compelling acceptance; this is an addition forced by evidence. The author notes that most later Sabians (philosophers) mix their philosophy with monotheism (Hanifiyya), leading to confusion of truth and falsehood. He clarifies that 'Sabianism' in his usage means innovation without belief in prophethood, whereas ancient Sabians included monotheists who believed in God and the Last Day, like righteous Jews and Christians before Muhammad's mission. This critique underscores the Islamic theological perspective that logical classifications must be contextualized within divine guidance.

Key Terms
صابئة
مشهورات
حنيفية

Key Takeaway
Logic without prophetic guidance can lead to incomplete truth; Ibn Taymiyya urges that definitions must be rooted in divine revelation.

Haqq and Batil: Two Meanings
Author defines haqq and batil both existentially and practically.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the existential and practical senses of haqq and batil and apply them to Islamic examples.

Core Idea
Haqq means both 'established' and 'beneficial' depending on context.

This passage clarifies that the terms haqq and batil have two distinct yet complementary meanings. In one sense, they refer to existence and non-existence. In another, they refer to the effectiveness or futility of actions. Understanding this duality is essential for interpreting theological and legal discourse where the same term may shift meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contexts
Read the passage and note that haqq and batil are used in two different contexts: one related to existence (النفي والإثبات) and one related to actions (في الأفعال).
Existential: haqq = thabit, batil = muntasif. Practical: haqq = hasil li'l-maqsud, batil = la fa'idata fihi.
2
Distinguish existential from practical
Existential haqq/batil deals with what is real or unreal. Practical haqq/batil deals with whether an action achieves its purpose.
A proposition can be haqq in the existential sense if it corresponds to reality; an action can be haqq if it fulfills its intended goal.
3
Apply to Islamic examples
Think of an example from Kalam for the existential sense (e.g., Allah's existence is haqq) and from Fiqh for the practical sense (e.g., a valid prayer is haqq).
Ensure the example clearly matches the context described in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا كان الحق والباطل يطلق تارة بمعنى: النفي والإثبات، فيقال: هذا حق أي ثابت، وهذا باطل أي منتف. وفي الأفعال بمعنى: التحصيل للمقصود، فيقال: هذا الفعل حقٌّ أي نافع أو محصل للمقصود، ويقال: باطل أي لا فائدة فيه ونحو ذلك.
For this reason, 'haqq' and 'batil' are sometimes used in the sense of negation and affirmation: it is said 'this is haqq' meaning established, and 'this is batil' meaning negated. And in actions, in the sense of achieving the intended purpose: it is said 'this action is haqq' meaning beneficial or achieving the intended purpose, and 'batil' meaning there is no benefit in it, and so on.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage defines the terms 'haqq' and 'batil' by distinguishing two contexts. In the existential context, haqq means something that is firmly established (thabit) and batil means something that is non-existent (muntasif). For example, in Kalam, the existence of the Creator is haqq. In the practical context, haqq refers to an action that achieves its intended goal (hasil li'l-maqsud), while batil refers to a futile action. For instance, a valid prayer is haqq, while an invalid one is batil. This dual usage is important for understanding later dialectical arguments where the same term may shift meaning.

Key Terms
الحق
الباطل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) In existential context
B) In practical context
C) In both contexts
D) In propositional logic

Key Takeaway
Haqq and batil have two meanings: existential (established/non-existent) and practical (beneficial/futile), and context determines which applies.

?

Critique of Prophecy as Intuitive Knowledge
Author critiques philosophers' reduction of prophecy to intuition and analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the philosophical reduction of prophethood to intuitive knowledge and identify its epistemological grounds.

Core Idea
Prophethood is not a natural faculty of intuition; it is a divine selection that transcends human analogy.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya takes on the philosophers' claim that prophethood is a form of intuitive knowledge (hads) arising from the purity of the soul. He argues that this reduces prophethood to a natural ability shared by many, stripping it of its divine character. The lesson will guide you through his critique and its implications for Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Philosophical Claim
Locate in the Arabic where the philosophers define prophethood as intuitive knowledge based on soul purity and strength.
The author uses 'جعل علوم الأنبياء من العلوم الحَدْسِية' to introduce the target claim.
2
Extract Ibn Taymiyya's Objections
Find his arguments: intuition reduces to analogical reasoning (qiyas al-tamthil), visions are mere dreams, and common people have similar experiences.
Look for 'أن الحَدْسَ راجع إلى قياس التمثيل' and 'هذا القدر يحصل مثله لكثير من عوام الناس'.
3
Understand the Alternative View
Ibn Taymiyya implies prophethood is a divine gift, not acquired, involving direct angelic communication and selection by Allah.
He criticizes the idea that prophethood is 'مكتسبة' (acquired) and denies the philosophical doubt about Allah speaking to Musa.
4
Evaluate the Critique
Assess whether Ibn Taymiyya's objections are logically sound and grounded in revelation. Consider the consequences he warns of: arrogance and disbelief.
He concludes that those who follow this path become 'من أجهل الناس وأظلمهم' (most ignorant and unjust).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الأول، فإنه جعل علوم الأنبياء من العلوم الحَدْسِية؛ لقوة صفاء تلك النفوس القُدسية وطهارتها، وأن قوى النفوس في الحدس لا تقفُ عنـد حد، ولا بد للعالم من نظام يَنْصِبُه حكيم، فيعطي النفوس المؤيدة من القوَّة ما تعلم به ما لا يعلمه غيرها بطريق الحَدْس، ويتمثل لها ما تسمعه وتراه في نفسها من الكلام ومن الملائكة ما لا يسمعه غيرها، ويكون لها من القوَّة العملية التي تطيعها بها هَيُولى العالم ما ليس لغيرها. فهذه الخوارقُ في قوى العلم، مع السمع والبصر، وقوة العمل والقدرة، هي النبوة عندهم. ومعلوم أن الحَدْسَ راجع إلى قياس التمثيل كما تقدم، وأما ما يسمع ويرى في نفسه فهو من جنس الرؤيا، وهذا القدر يحصل مثله لكثير من عوام الناس وكفَّارهم، فضلا عن أولياء الله وأنبيائه، فكيف يُجْعَلُ ذلك هو غاية النبوَّة؟! وإن كان الذي يثبتونه للأنبياء أكمل وأشرف فهو كمَلِكِ أقوى مِن مَلِك. ولهذا صاروا يقولون: النبوَّة مكتسبة، ولم يثبتوا نزول ملائكة من عند الله إلى من يختارُه ويصطفيه من عباده، ولا قَصْدَه لتكليم شخص معين من رسله، كما يُذْكَر عن بعض قدمائهم أنه قال لموسى بن عمران: أنا أصدقك في كلّ شيءٍ إلا في أن علَّة العِلل كلَّمَك، ما أقدِرُ أن أصدقك في هذا! ولهذا صار من ضلَّ بمثل هذا الكلام يدَّعي مساواة الأنبياء والمرسلين أو التقدم عليهم، وهذا كثير في كثير من الناس الذين يعتقدون في أنفسهم أنهم أكمل النوع، وهم من أجهل الناس وأظلمهم وأكفّرهم وأعظمهم نفاقاً.
As for the first, they made the sciences of the prophets from the intuitive sciences, because of the strength of the purity of those holy souls and their cleanliness, and that the powers of souls in intuition do not stop at a limit, and the world must have a system that a wise [being] sets up, so that the supported souls are given from the power by which they know what others do not know by way of intuition, and what they hear and see in themselves of speech and angels that others do not hear is represented to them, and they have from the practical power that the matter of the world obeys them what others do not have. So these marvels in the powers of knowledge, along with hearing and sight, and the power of action and ability, are prophethood according to them. And it is known that intuition goes back to analogical reasoning as previously mentioned, and as for what one hears and sees in oneself, it is of the kind of dreams, and this amount occurs similarly to many common people and their disbelievers, not to mention the saints of Allah and His prophets, so how can that be made the ultimate goal of prophethood?! And if what they affirm for the prophets is more perfect and honorable, then it is like a stronger king compared to a king. That is why they say: prophethood is acquired, and they do not affirm the descent of angels from Allah to whom He chooses and selects from His servants, nor His intending to speak to a specific person from His messengers, as it is mentioned from some of their ancients that he said to Musa ibn 'Imran: 'I believe you in everything except that the Cause of causes spoke to you; I cannot believe you in this!' And that is why whoever goes astray with such speech claims equality with the prophets and messengers or precedence over them, and this is frequent among many people who believe in themselves that they are the most perfect of the species, while they are among the most ignorant, most unjust, most disbelieving, and most hypocritical of people.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is a critique of the philosophers' view that prophethood is a kind of intuitive knowledge (hads). The author (Ibn Taymiyya) explains that they attribute prophetic knowledge to the strength of holy souls and their ability to receive intuitive insights. They claim that these souls have such powerful intuition that they can learn what others cannot, and they see and hear angels in themselves. The author then argues that intuition is actually reducible to analogical reasoning (qiyas al-tamthil), and the visions are merely dreams, which even common people and disbelievers experience. Therefore, reducing prophethood to these natural faculties diminishes its divine nature. The author further notes that this leads to the claim that prophethood is acquired, denying the unique selection and inspiration by Allah. He gives an example of a philosopher who doubted that Allah could directly speak to Moses. Finally, he warns that such views lead to arrogance and even disbelief.

Key Terms
الحدس
النبوة
قياس التمثيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Intuition is superior to analogical reasoning.
B) Intuition is reducible to analogical reasoning.
C) Intuition is independent of reasoning.
D) Analogical reasoning is a type of intuition.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya argues that reducing prophethood to intuition and analogy strips it of its divine character, leading to disbelief and arrogance.

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Logicians' Epistemological Monopoly
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the claim that all certain knowledge must come through logical syllogisms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's primary objection to the logicians' claim that syllogism is the exclusive path to certain knowledge, and distinguish his criticism from outright rejection of logic.

Core Idea
Syllogism is not the only scale: claimers of epistemic monopoly are ignorant, unjust, and disbelieving.

In this passage from Naqd al-Mantiq, Ibn Taymiyya launches a scathing critique against those who assert that all certain knowledge is attained only through Aristotelian syllogisms. He warns that such a view leads to equating oneself with prophets or even claiming superiority—a sign of ignorance and hypocrisy. He then distinguishes the mutakallimun (rationalist theologians) who use syllogism in a more acceptable way, though they too inherit flaws from Greek logic. Understanding this critique is essential for appreciating the Islamic epistemological tradition that values prophetic knowledge as a source beyond human reason.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target claim
Find the exact assertion Ibn Taymiyya is attacking: that all certain knowledge must come through the logicians' syllogism. Look for phrases like 'يُعْلَمُ بهذا القياس' (by this syllogism we know).
The claim is implicit in the logicians' practice; Ibn Taymiyya explicitly criticizes those who go astray by such speech.
2
Examine the consequences of accepting the claim
Notice Ibn Taymiyya's harsh characterization: those who hold this view claim equality with prophets or even precedence. He calls them the most ignorant, unjust, and hypocritical of people.
This ethical criticism shows the practical dangers of the epistemological error.
3
Analyze his treatment of the mutakallimun
Observe that he distinguishes the rationalist theologians: their use of syllogism is closer to the method of believing scholars, but still contains falsehoods inherited from logicians or invented by themselves.
Ibn Taymiyya is not condemning all use of syllogism, only the claim of monopoly.
4
Determine the author's overall stance
Conclude that Ibn Taymiyya is not rejecting syllogism outright, but critiquing the claim that it is the only path to certain knowledge. He is refining the scope of logic, not abolishing it.
This is a critical refinement, not a wholesale rejection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا صار من ضلَّ بمثل هذا الكلام يدَّعي مساواة الأنبياء والمرسلين أو التقدم عليهم، وهذا كثير في كثير من الناس الذين يعتقدون في أنفسهم أنهم أكمل النوع، وهم من أجهل الناس وأظلمهم وأكفرهم وأعظمهم نفاقاً. وأما المتكلمون المنطقيون، فيقولون: يُعْلَمُ بهذا القياس ثبوت الصانع، وقدرته، وجواز إرسال الرسل، وتأييده لهم بما يوجب تصديقهم فيما يقولونه. وهذه الطريقة أقرب إلى طريقة العلماء المؤمنين، وإن كان قد يكونُ فيها أنواع من الباطل، تارةً من جهة ما تَقَلَّدوه عن المنطقيين، وتارةً من جهة ما ابتدعوه هم، مما ليس هذا موضعه. ومنطقية اليهود والنصارى كذلك، لكنَّ الهدى والعلم والبيان في فلاسفة المسلمين ومتكلميهم أعظم منه في أهل الكتابين؛ لما في تَيْنِكَ الملتين من الفساد. ولكن الغرض تقرير جنس النبوَّات؛ فإن أهل الملل متفقون عليها، لكن اليهود والنصارى آمنوا ببعض الرُّسل وكفروا ببعض، والصابئة الفلاسفة ونحوهم آمنوا ببعض صفات الرسالة دون بعض، فإذا أتفق متفلسف من أهل الكتاب جَمَع الكُفْرَين الكفر بخاتم المرسلين، والكفر بحقائق صفات الرسالة في جميع المرسلين. فهذا هذا. فيقال لهم ـ مع علمهم بتفاوت قوى بني آدم في الإدراك : ما المانع من أن يخرق سمع أحدهم وبصره فيسمع ويرى من الأمور الموجودة في الخارج ما لا يراه غيره ؟ كما قال النبي : «إني أرى ما لا ترون، وأسمعُ ما لا تسمعون، أَطَّت السَّماءُ وحُقَّ لها أن تنط، ما فيها موضعُ أربع أصابع إلا وملك قائمٌ أو قاعد أو راكع أو ساجد»، فهذا إحساس بالظاهر أو الباطن لما هو في الخارج. وكذلك العلوم الكلية البديهية قد علمتم أنها ليس لها حد في بني آدم، فمن أين لكم أن بعض النفوس ما يكون لها من العلوم البديهية التي يختص بها أو بها وبأمثالها ما لا يكون من البديهيات عندكم؟ وإذا كان هذا ممكنا وعامة أهل الأرض على أنه واقع لغير الأنبياء، دع الأنبياء فمثل هذه العلوم ليس في منطقكم طريق إليها؛ إذ ليست من المشهورات ولا الجدلية ولا موادها عندكم يقينية، وأنتم لا تعلمون نفيها، وجمهور أهل الأرض من الأولين والآخرين على إثباتها، فإن كذَّبتم بها كنتم مع الكفر والتكذيب بالحق، وخسارة الدنيا والآخرة تاركين لمنطقكم أيضًا، وخارجين عمّا أوجبتموه على أنفسكم أنكم لا تقولون إلا بموجب القياس؛ إذ ليس لهم بهذا النفي قياس ولا حجة تُذكر، ولهذا لم يذكروا عليه حجة، وإنما أندرج هذا النفي في كلامهم بغير حجة. وإن قلتم : بل هي حق، اعترفتم بأن من الحق ما لا يوزن بميزان منطقكم.
Thus it is that one who goes astray by such speech claims equality with the prophets and messengers, or precedence over them. This is common among many people who believe themselves to be the most perfect of the species, while they are among the most ignorant, most unjust, most disbelieving, and most hypocritical of people. As for the rationalist theologians, they say: By this syllogism we know the existence of the Maker, His power, the permissibility of sending messengers, and His supporting them with what necessitates believing them in what they say. This method is closer to the method of believing scholars, although it may contain types of falsehood, sometimes from what they imitated from the logicians, and sometimes from what they themselves innovated, which is not the place for this. The logicians among Jews and Christians are likewise, but guidance, knowledge, and clarity among the Muslim philosophers and theologians are greater than among the People of the Two Books, because of the corruption in those two religions. But the purpose is to establish the genus of prophecies; for the people of all religions agree on it, but Jews and Christians believe in some messengers and disbelieve in others, and the Sabian philosophers and the like believe in some attributes of the message but not others. So if a philosopher from among the People of the Book comes together, he combines the two disbeliefs: disbelief in the Seal of the Messengers and disbelief in the realities of the attributes of the message in all messengers. So this is it. So it is said to them — while they know the variation in the powers of human beings in perception: What prevents that the hearing and sight of one of them be split open, so that he hears and sees of existing matters in the external world what others do not see? As the Prophet said: 'Indeed, I see what you do not see, and I hear what you do not hear. The heaven groaned, and it is right that it groans. There is no space of four fingers except that there is an angel standing, kneeling, bowing, or prostrating.' So this is a sensory perception, outwardly or inwardly, of what is in the external world. Likewise, the universal intuitive sciences — you already know that they have no limit among human beings. So how do you know that some souls may have from the intuitive sciences, which they are specialized in, or in them and the like, what is not among your intuitives? And if this is possible — and the majority of the people of the earth believe it occurs for non-prophets, let alone prophets — then such sciences have no path to them in your logic; for they are not among the widely known (mashhurat) nor the dialectical (jadaliyya), nor are their materials certain with you, and you do not know their negation. The majority of the people of the earth, from the first and the last, affirm them. So if you deny them, you are with disbelief and denial of the truth, and the loss of this world and the Hereafter, forsaking your logic as well, and going outside what you have obligated upon yourselves that you only speak by means of the syllogism; for you have no syllogism for this negation nor any mentionable proof. That is why they did not mention a proof for it. Rather, this negation came embedded in their speech without proof. And if you say: Rather, it is true, then you admit that among truth is what cannot be weighed by the scale of your logic.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya against the logicians' claim that all certain knowledge is attained only through their syllogistic reasoning. He begins by criticizing those who, influenced by such reasoning, equate themselves with prophets or even claim superiority — these are the ignorant hypocrites. He then acknowledges that the rationalist theologians (mutakallimun) use syllogisms to prove the existence of God, His power, and the possibility of prophethood, which is closer to the method of believing scholars, though it still contains falsehoods inherited from Greek logic or invented by themselves. Next, he notes that logicians among Jews and Christians hold similar views, but Muslim philosophers and theologians are superior because of the greater truth in Islam. However, his main objective is to establish the genus of prophethood itself, which all religions agree on in some form, though they differ in specifics. He then launches a key epistemological argument: given the known variation in human perceptual and intellectual powers, why cannot a person have extraordinary sensory perception (like the Prophet seeing and hearing angels) or intuitive knowledge that others lack? He cites the hadith of the Prophet describing what he sees and hears. He argues that universal intuitive sciences (al-‘ulum al-kulliyya al-badihiyya) have no fixed limit among humans; thus some souls may possess intuitive knowledge that is not intuitive for others. Since this is possible and widely affirmed, such knowledge cannot be reached by the logicians' methods (since it is neither mashhurat nor jadal, nor certain for them). They cannot prove its non-existence. If they deny it, they disbelieve and contradict their own principle of only following syllogistic proof. If they affirm it, they admit that truth exists beyond their logical scale.

Key Terms

البديهية
المشهورات

Ibn Taymiyya argues that the logicians' claim of epistemic monopoly over certain knowledge is not only false but also morally dangerous, as it undermines prophetic authority.

The Possibility of Extraordinary Intuitive Knowledge
Ibn Taymiyya argues for the possibility of intuitive knowledge beyond syllogism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument that intuitive knowledge exceeds the logicians' syllogistic method, using his evidence from the variation in human powers and the Prophet's hadith.

Core Idea
Because human powers vary, some may have intuitive knowledge beyond the syllogism's reach.

Continuing his critique, Ibn Taymiyya now presents a constructive epistemological argument. He points to the undeniable variation in human perceptual and intellectual capacities: why should it be impossible for a person—especially a prophet—to have sensory or intuitive knowledge that others lack? He supports this with a hadith in which the Prophet describes seeing and hearing angels. He also argues that the so-called universal intuitive sciences (badihiyyat) are not fixed; what is intuitive for one may not be for another. Thus, the logicians cannot claim that all certain knowledge must pass through their syllogism, because there is knowledge that they cannot access via their own methods.

Guided Path
1
Identify Ibn Taymiyya's key question to the logicians
Look for the rhetorical question beginning with 'ما المانع' (What prevents...). He asks: what prevents that someone's hearing and sight be opened to perceive external things others do not see?
This sets up the argument that extraordinary perception is possible.
2
Locate his evidence from hadith
Find the hadith quotation: 'إني أرى ما لا ترون...' (Indeed, I see what you do not see...). The Prophet describes seeing angels and hearing the heaven groan.
This is a concrete example of knowledge beyond normal human perception.
3
Understand the variability of intuitive knowledge
Read the claim: 'العلوم الكلية البديهية... ليس لها حد في بني آدم' (The universal intuitive sciences have no limit among human beings). Ibn Taymiyya argues that what is intuitive for some may not be for others.
This challenges the logicians' assumption that badihiyyat are universal and fixed.
4
Connect to the logicians' categories
Note that such knowledge is not in the logicians' sources: it is not among the mashhurat (widely accepted) nor jadal (dialectical), nor are its premises certain for them. They cannot prove its negation.
Therefore, their logic cannot access or refute this knowledge.
5
Evaluate the conclusion
Consider the two options for the logicians: if they deny it, they have no proof and contradict their own principle; if they affirm it, they admit that truth exists beyond their logical scale.
Ibn Taymiyya forces a dilemma that undermines the claim of monopoly.

Source Text

ولهذا صار من ضلَّ بمثل هذا الكلام يدَّعي مساواة الأنبياء والمرسلين أو التقدم عليهم، وهذا كثير في كثير من الناس الذين يعتقدون في أنفسهم أنهم أكمل النوع، وهم من أجهل الناس وأظلمهم وأكفرهم وأعظمهم نفاقاً. وأما المتكلمون المنطقيون، فيقولون: يُعْلَمُ بهذا القياس ثبوت الصانع، وقدرته، وجواز إرسال الرسل، وتأييده لهم بما يوجب تصديقهم فيما يقولونه. وهذه الطريقة أقرب إلى طريقة العلماء المؤمنين، وإن كان قد يكونُ فيها أنواع من الباطل، تارةً من جهة ما تَقَلَّدوه عن المنطقيين، وتارةً من جهة ما ابتدعوه هم، مما ليس هذا موضعه. ومنطقية اليهود والنصارى كذلك، لكنَّ الهدى والعلم والبيان في فلاسفة المسلمين ومتكلميهم أعظم منه في أهل الكتابين؛ لما في تَيْنِكَ الملتين من الفساد. ولكن الغرض تقرير جنس النبوَّات؛ فإن أهل الملل متفقون عليها، لكن اليهود والنصارى آمنوا ببعض الرُّسل وكفروا ببعض، والصابئة الفلاسفة ونحوهم آمنوا ببعض صفات الرسالة دون بعض، فإذا أتفق متفلسف من أهل الكتاب جَمَع الكُفْرَين الكفر بخاتم المرسلين، والكفر بحقائق صفات الرسالة في جميع المرسلين. فهذا هذا. فيقال لهم ـ مع علمهم بتفاوت قوى بني آدم في الإدراك : ما المانع من أن يخرق سمع أحدهم وبصره فيسمع ويرى من الأمور الموجودة في الخارج ما لا يراه غيره ؟ كما قال النبي : «إني أرى ما لا ترون، وأسمعُ ما لا تسمعون، أَطَّت السَّماءُ وحُقَّ لها أن تنط، ما فيها موضعُ أربع أصابع إلا وملك قائمٌ أو قاعد أو راكع أو ساجد»، فهذا إحساس بالظاهر أو الباطن لما هو في الخارج. وكذلك العلوم الكلية البديهية قد علمتم أنها ليس لها حد في بني آدم، فمن أين لكم أن بعض النفوس ما يكون لها من العلوم البديهية التي يختص بها أو بها وبأمثالها ما لا يكون من البديهيات عندكم؟ وإذا كان هذا ممكنا وعامة أهل الأرض على أنه واقع لغير الأنبياء، دع الأنبياء فمثل هذه العلوم ليس في منطقكم طريق إليها؛ إذ ليست من المشهورات ولا الجدلية ولا موادها عندكم يقينية، وأنتم لا تعلمون نفيها، وجمهور أهل الأرض من الأولين والآخرين على إثباتها، فإن كذَّبتم بها كنتم مع الكفر والتكذيب بالحق، وخسارة الدنيا والآخرة تاركين لمنطقكم أيضًا، وخارجين عمّا أوجبتموه على أنفسكم أنكم لا تقولون إلا بموجب القياس؛ إذ ليس لهم بهذا النفي قياس ولا حجة تُذكر، ولهذا لم يذكروا عليه حجة، وإنما أندرج هذا النفي في كلامهم بغير حجة. وإن قلتم : بل هي حق، اعترفتم بأن من الحق ما لا يوزن بميزان منطقكم.
Thus it is that one who goes astray by such speech claims equality with the prophets and messengers, or precedence over them. This is common among many people who believe themselves to be the most perfect of the species, while they are among the most ignorant, most unjust, most disbelieving, and most hypocritical of people. As for the rationalist theologians, they say: By this syllogism we know the existence of the Maker, His power, the permissibility of sending messengers, and His supporting them with what necessitates believing them in what they say. This method is closer to the method of believing scholars, although it may contain types of falsehood, sometimes from what they imitated from the logicians, and sometimes from what they themselves innovated, which is not the place for this. The logicians among Jews and Christians are likewise, but guidance, knowledge, and clarity among the Muslim philosophers and theologians are greater than among the People of the Two Books, because of the corruption in those two religions. But the purpose is to establish the genus of prophecies; for the people of all religions agree on it, but Jews and Christians believe in some messengers and disbelieve in others, and the Sabian philosophers and the like believe in some attributes of the message but not others. So if a philosopher from among the People of the Book comes together, he combines the two disbeliefs: disbelief in the Seal of the Messengers and disbelief in the realities of the attributes of the message in all messengers. So this is it. So it is said to them — while they know the variation in the powers of human beings in perception: What prevents that the hearing and sight of one of them be split open, so that he hears and sees of existing matters in the external world what others do not see? There is no space of four fingers except that there is an angel standing, kneeling, bowing, or prostrating.' So this is a sensory perception, outwardly or inwardly, of what is in the external world. Likewise, the universal intuitive sciences — you already know that they have no limit among human beings. So how do you know that some souls may have from the intuitive sciences, which they are specialized in, or in them and the like, what is not among your intuitives? And if this is possible — and the majority of the people of the earth believe it occurs for non-prophets, let alone prophets — then such sciences have no path to them in your logic; for they are not among the widely known (mashhurat) nor the dialectical (jadaliyya), nor are their materials certain with you, and you do not know their negation. The majority of the people of the earth, from the first and the last, affirm them. So if you deny them, you are with disbelief and denial of the truth, and the loss of this world and the Hereafter, forsaking your logic as well, and going outside what you have obligated upon yourselves that you only speak by means of the syllogism; for you have no syllogism for this negation nor any mentionable proof. That is why they did not mention a proof for it. Rather, this negation came embedded in their speech without proof. And if you say: Rather, it is true, then you admit that among truth is what cannot be weighed by the scale of your logic.

Reconstructing Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Logic's Scale
Author challenges logicians that their scale cannot weigh the greatest matters like prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's critique of logic's failure to weigh prophethood and evaluate its internal validity.

Core Idea
Ibn Taymiyya's target is not logic itself—it is the claim that Greek formalism is epistemologically supreme over prophetic knowledge.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya deploys a devastating rhetorical critique against the claim that logic can serve as a universal scale for all truth. He zeros in on the highest subject—prophethood—and shows that logic falls silent or becomes contradictory. As you work through the passage, you will learn to identify the structure of his argument and assess its logical force.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target claim
What claim about logic are the logicians making that Ibn Taymiyya attacks? Find the underlying assumption he is demolishing.
The logicians claim logic is the standard of true sciences and certain wisdom.
2
Extract the central analogy
Ibn Taymiyya compares the scale of logic to scales for wealth. What does this analogy reveal about the purpose of a scale? What is the 'gold' in this context?
Prophethood is the gold—the most valuable knowledge.
3
Analyze the trilemma
The author presents a three-pronged challenge: if logicians affirm, deny, or doubt, logic fails. Trace each horn and see why it leads to a contradiction.
Logic cannot agree whether prophethood is true or false, so it is either indifferent or contradictory.
4
Assess the internal validity
Does the critique itself rely on any assumptions? Is the analogy sound? Could a logician respond? Evaluate the strength of the argument.
Consider if the critique is itself a logical argument against logic's universality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن قلتم لا ندري أحقِّ هي أم باطل؟ أعترفتم بأن أعظم المطالب وأجلَّها لا يوزنُ بميزان المنطق. فإن صدقتم لم يوافقكم المنطق، وإن كَذَّبتم لم يوافقكم المنطق، وإن أرتبتُم لم ينفعكم المنطق! ومن المعلوم أن موازين الأموال لا يُقصد أن يوزن بها الحطب والرَّصاصُ دون الذهب والفضة، وأمرُ النبوَّات وما جاءت به الرُّسل أعظمُ في العلوم من الذهب في الأموال، فإذا لم يكن في منطقكم ميزان له كان الميزانُ مع أنه ميزان عائل جائز هو أيضًا عاجز، فهو ميزان جاهل ظالم؛ هو إما أن يرد الحق ويدفعه فيكون ظالما، أو لا يزنه ولا يبين أمره فيكون جاهلا، أو يجتمع فيه الأمران فيرد الحق ويدفعه، وهو الحق الذي ليس للنفوس عنه عوض، ولا عنه مندوحة، وليست سعادتها إلا فيه ولا هلاكها إلا تركه. فكيف يستقيم مع هذا أن تقولوا: إنه وما وزنتموه به من المتاع الخسيس الذي أنتم في وزنكم إيَّاه به ظالمون عائلون، لم تزنوا بالقسطاس المستقيم، و لم تستدلُّوا بالآيات البينات ـ هو معيار العلوم الحقيقية، والحكمة اليقينية، التي فاز بالسَّعادة عالمُها، وخاب بالشَّقاوة جاهلُها؟! ورأسُ مال السَّادة وغايةُ العالم المنصف منكم أن يعترف بعجز ميزانكم عنه، وأما عوام علمائكم فيكذبون به ويردونه، وإن كان منطقكم يَرُدُّ عليهم، فلستُم بتحريف أمر منطقكم بأحسن حالا من اليهود والنصارى في تحريف كتاب الله الذي هو في الأصل حقٌّ هادٍ لا ريب فيه، فهذا هذا.
And if you say: 'We do not know whether it is true or false?' You have admitted that the greatest and most noble of questions are not weighed by the scale of logic. For if you affirm it, logic does not agree with you; if you deny it, logic does not agree with you; and if you doubt it, logic does not benefit you! And it is known that the scales of wealth are not intended to weigh wood and lead instead of gold and silver, and the matter of prophethood and what the messengers brought is greater in the sciences than gold in wealth. So if there is no scale in your logic for it, then the scale, even though it is a biased scale, is also incapable; so it is an ignorant, unjust scale. It either repels the truth and pushes it away, so it is unjust; or it does not weigh it and does not clarify its matter, so it is ignorant; or both are combined in it, so it repels the truth and pushes it away. And it is the truth from which souls have no substitute, nor any escape, and their happiness is only in it and their destruction is only in abandoning it. How then is it consistent with this that you say: 'Indeed, it (logic) and what you weigh with it of base goods—while you are in weighing it unjust and biased, you have not weighed with the straight balance, nor have you sought guidance from clear signs—is the criterion of the true sciences and certain wisdom, whose knower triumphs in happiness and whose ignorant fails in misery?' And the capital of the masters and the goal of the fair-minded scholar among you is to admit the incapacity of your scale for it. As for the common folk of your scholars, they deny it and reject it. And even if your logic refutes them, you are, by distorting the matter of your logic, in no better state than the Jews and Christians in distorting the Book of God, which is originally truth and guidance with no doubt in it. So this is that.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a rhetorical critique of logic's inability to handle the most important truths, specifically prophethood. The author begins by addressing the logicians: if they claim ignorance about whether something is true or false, they admit that the greatest questions are not weighed by their logic. Then they are trapped: whether they affirm, deny, or doubt, logic fails them. He then compares the scale of logic to a scale for wealth: just as a scale for wealth is not meant to weigh wood or lead, but gold and silver, so the scale of logic should weigh the most valuable knowledge—prophethood. But since it cannot, it is biased, ignorant, and unjust. It either rejects truth or fails to weigh it. The author then questions how logicians can claim that logic is the standard of true sciences when they themselves are unjust in their weighing and do not use clear signs. He concludes that the fair-minded among them admit the incapacity, but the common scholars deny it, and by distorting logic they are like Jews and Christians distorting scripture.

Key Terms
ميزان المنطق
عائل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it weighs wood and lead instead of gold and silver.
B) Because it either repels the truth or fails to weigh it, or both.
C) Because logicians are dishonest.
D) Because it cannot weigh prophethood at all.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya argues that the scale of logic is fundamentally incapable and biased when applied to the greatest truths like prophethood, undermining the logicians' claim that it is the universal criterion of knowledge.

Medicine and Logic: Ibn Taymiyya's Empirical Counterexample
Ibn Taymiyya argues that medicine predates logic and thrives without it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn Taymiyya's historical argument that sound knowledge (like medicine) can be achieved without the philosopher's logical art.

Core Idea
Sound knowledge predates Greek logic and proves its dispensability.

Ibn Taymiyya opens this passage by citing the medical tradition. He points out that Hippocrates made widely accepted statements that were empirically confirmed, and he lived before the founder of Aristotelian logic. This is not a casual remark—it is a direct challenge to the philosophers' claim that logic is the indispensable tool for all certain knowledge. Ibn Taymiyya wants us to recognize that entire fields of certain knowledge existed and thrived without ever using the formal syllogistic method.

Guided Path
1
Identify the historical figure and field
Find whom Ibn Taymiyya refers to by 'he' in the first sentence. The context indicates Hippocrates and the field of medicine. Note that his statements were 'accepted by the medical community' and 'found their confirmation through experiments.'
2
Observe the temporal precedence
Ibn Taymiyya explicitly says this person was not aided by the art of logic and was 'before its founder.' This means the knowledge was acquired without the philosophical tool of qiyas.
The 'founder' likely refers to Aristotle, though Ibn Taymiyya does not name him.
3
Extract the epistemological implication
The implication is that if medicine—a science that yields certain and beneficial knowledge—was developed without logic, then logic is not a necessary condition for sound knowledge. This undercuts the philosophers' claim that logic is the sole instrument for valid reasoning.
This is a historical counterexample against logical foundationalism.

له فيها من الكلام الذي تلقاه أهل الطب بالقبول ووجدوا مصداقه بالتجارب، وله فيها من القضايا الكلية التي عند عقلاء بني آدم من أعظم الأمور، ومع هذا فليس هو مستعينا بشيء من هذه الصناعة، بل كان قبل واضعها. وهم وإن كان العلم الطبيعي عندهم أعظم وأعلى من علم الطب فلا ريب أنه متصل به فبالعلم بطبائع الأجسام المعينة المحسوسة تعلم طبائع سائر الأجسام، ومبدأ الحركة والسكون الذي في الجسم، ويستدل بالجزء على الكل، ولهذا كثيرًا ما يتناظرون في مسائل ويتنازع فيها هؤلاء وهؤلاء، كتناظر الفقهاء والمتكلمين في مسائل كثيرة تتّفق فيها الصناعتان، وأولئك يدعون عموم النظر، ولكن الخطأ والغلط عند المتكلمين والمتفلسفة أكثر مما هو عند الفقهاء والأطباء، وكلامهم وعلمهم أنفع، وأولئك أكثر ضلالا وأقل نفعا؛ لأنهم طلبوا بالقياس ما لا يعلم بالقياس، وزاحموا الفطرة والنبوة مزاحمة أوجبت من مخالفتهم للفطرة والنبوة ما صاروا به من شياطين الإنس والجن الذين يوحي بعضهم إلى بعض زخرف القول غرورا، بخلاف الطب المحض فإنه علم نافع، وكذلك الفقه المحض.
He has in it (medicine) statements that the medical community accepted and found their confirmation through experiments. He has in it universal propositions that are among the greatest matters for the rational people of mankind. Yet he was not aided by anything from this art (logic); rather, he was before its founder. And even though natural science, in their view, is greater and higher than the science of medicine, there is no doubt that it is connected to it. For by knowing the specific natures of sensible bodies, the natures of other bodies are known, as well as the principle of motion and rest in a body, and one infers from the part to the whole. Therefore, they often debate issues and dispute over them, just as jurists and theologians debate in many issues where the two disciplines concur. Those (theologians and philosophers) claim generality of theoretical reasoning, but error and mistake among theologians and philosophers is more than among jurists and physicians. Their speech and knowledge is more beneficial, and those (theologians/philosophers) are more astray and less beneficial because they sought through qiyas what cannot be known by qiyas, and they opposed fitra and prophethood in a way that caused their opposition to fitra and prophethood to make them devils of humans and jinn who inspire each other with delusive speech. In contrast, pure medicine is beneficial knowledge, and likewise pure fiqh.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a critical comparison by Ibn Taymiyya between practical sciences (medicine and fiqh) and speculative disciplines (theology and philosophy). He begins by noting that Hippocrates' medical statements were accepted and empirically confirmed, even though he predated the art of logic. This shows that sound knowledge does not depend on Aristotelian logic. He then acknowledges that natural science (physics) is considered higher than medicine, but it is connected to it: understanding specific physical bodies leads to knowledge of general principles and inference from part to whole. However, he points out that debates between jurists and theologians often occur, but error is more common among theologians and philosophers. Their speech is less beneficial because they attempt to use analogical reasoning (qiyas) to reach knowledge that cannot be attained that way, and they contradict human nature (fitra) and prophetic guidance. This opposition turns them into sources of deception. In contrast, pure medicine and pure fiqh are genuinely beneficial sciences.

Checkpoint
What is Ibn Taymiyya's main point about the medical tradition in this passage?
A) Medicine is inferior to natural science.
B) Medicine was developed after the invention of logic.
C) Medicine achieved reliable knowledge without using the logical art of the philosophers.
D) Medicine is the most beneficial science.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya uses the historical example of medicine to argue that certain knowledge can be attained without the philosopher's logical method, thus undermining the necessity of Aristotelian logic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find an example from Islamic history (not medicine) where a scholar achieved certain knowledge without using formal Aristotelian logic. Briefly describe the evidence that this knowledge was sound.
?
Reflect on Ibn Taymiyya's argument: Does the fact that Hippocrates predated logic prove that logic is unnecessary for all sciences? What might a logician respond?
